<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">"EU" redirects here. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/EU_(disambiguation)" title="EU (disambiguation)">EU (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about the European Union. For the various levels of integration within European countries including EU member states, see <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a>.</div>

Universal Time">UTC</a><span class="nowrap"> to UTC+2</span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Western_European_Time" title="Western European Time">WET</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_European_Time" title="Central European Time">CET</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_European_Time" title="Eastern European Time">EET</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th class="infobox-label" scope="row"><div class="ib-country-fake-li">• Summer (<a href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight saving time">DST</a>)</div></th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a><span class="nowrap">+1 to UTC+3</span></span> (<a href="/wiki/Western_European_Summer_Time" title="Western European href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/.eu" title=".eu">.eu</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[b]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2"><div class="ib-country-website"><b>Website</b><br/><span class="url"><a class="external text" href="http://europa.eu" rel="nofollow">europa<wbr/>.eu</a></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>European Union</b> (<b>EU</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Supranational_union" title="Supranational union">supranational</a> <a href="/wiki/Political_union" title="Political union">political</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_union" title="Economic union">economic union</a> of <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">27 member states</a> that are located primarily in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oecdcc_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-oecdcc-9">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[8]</a></sup> The union has a total area of 4,233,255.3 km<sup>2</sup> (1,634,469.0 sq mi) and an estimated total population of about 447<span class="nowrap"> </span>million. The EU has often been described as a <i><a href="/wiki/Sui_generis" title="Sui generis">sui generis</a></i> political entity (without precedent or comparison) combining the characteristics of both a federation and a confederation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>Containing 5.8<span class="nowrap"> </span>per cent of the <a href="/wiki/World_population" title="World population">world population</a> in 2020,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[c]</a></sup> the EU generated a nominal <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) of around <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$17.1</span><span class="nowrap"> </span>trillion in 2021,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GDP_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-GDP-4">[4]</a></sup> constituting approximately 18<span class="nowrap"> </span>per cent of global <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" title="Nominal GDP">nominal GDP</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[12]</a></sup> Additionally, all EU states have a very high <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> according to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Program" title="United Nations Development Program">United Nations Development Programme</a>.  Its cornerstone, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">Customs Union</a>, paved the way to establishing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Single_Market" title="European Single Market">an internal single market</a> based on standardised <a href="/wiki/European_Union_law" title="European Union law">legal framework and legislation</a> that applies in all member states in those matters, and only those matters, where the states have agreed to act as one. EU policies aim to ensure the free movement of people, goods, services and capital within the internal market;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Internal_Market_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Internal_Market-16">[13]</a></sup> enact legislation in justice and home affairs; and maintain common policies on <a href="/wiki/Common_Commercial_Policy_(EU)" title="Common Commercial Policy (EU)">trade</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">agriculture</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Common_Fisheries_Policy" title="Common Fisheries Policy">fisheries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Regional_policy_of_the_European_Union" title="Regional policy of the European Union">regional development</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[16]</a></sup> Passport controls have been abolished for travel within the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Internal_borders_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Internal_borders-20">[17]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> is a group composed of the 19 EU member states that have fully implemented  the <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_Monetary_Union_of_the_European_Union" title="Economic and Monetary Union of the European Union">economic and monetary union</a> and use the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro currency</a>. Through the <a href="/wiki/Common_Foreign_and_Security_Policy" title="Common Foreign and Security Policy">Common Foreign and Security Policy</a>, the union has developed a role in <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_European_Union" title="Foreign relations of the European Union">external relations</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_the_European_Union" title="Military of the European Union">defence</a>. It maintains permanent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_the_European_Union" title="List of diplomatic missions of the European Union">diplomatic missions</a> throughout the world and <a href="/wiki/European_Union_and_the_United_Nations" title="European Union and the United Nations">represents itself</a> at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_and_the_G7" title="European Union and the G7">G7</a> and the <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a>. Due to its global influence, the European Union has been described by some scholars as an <a href="/wiki/European_Union_as_an_emerging_superpower" title="European Union as an emerging superpower">emerging superpower</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcCormick2007_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcCormick2007-21">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>The union was established along with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_European_Union" title="Citizenship of the European Union">its citizenship</a> when the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a> came into force in 1993, and was subsequently incorporated as an  <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a> <a href="/wiki/Juridical_person" title="Juridical person">juridical person</a> upon entry into force of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a> in <a href="/wiki/2009" title="2009">2009</a>, <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECraigDe_Burca201115_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraigDe_Burca201115-24">[21]</a></sup> but its beginnings may be traced to its ealiest predecessors incorporated primarily by a group of founding states known as the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Six" title="Inner Six">Inner Six</a> (Belgium, France, Italy, Luxembourg, the Netherlands, and <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>) at the start of modern institutionalised <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a> in <a href="/wiki/1948" title="1948">1948</a> and onwards, namely to the <a href="/wiki/Western_Union_(alliance)" title="Western Union (alliance)">Western Union</a> (WU, 1954 renamed <a href="/wiki/Western_European_Union" title="Western European Union">Western European Union</a>, WEU) , the <a href="/wiki/International_Authority_for_the_Ruhr" title="International Authority for the Ruhr">International Authority for the Ruhr</a> (IAR), the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a> (ECSC), the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC, 1993 renamed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Community" title="European Community">European Community</a>, EC) and the <a href="/wiki/European_Atomic_Energy_Community" title="European Atomic Energy Community">European Atomic Energy Community</a> (Euratom), established, respectively, by the 1948 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brussels" title="Treaty of Brussels">Treaty of Brussels</a>, the 1948 <a href="/wiki/London_Six-Power_Conference" title="London Six-Power Conference">London Six-Power Conference</a>, the 1951 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1951)" title="Treaty of Paris (1951)">Treaty of Paris</a>, the 1957 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">Treaty of Rome</a> and the 1957 <a href="/wiki/Euratom_Treaty" title="Euratom Treaty">Euratom Treaty</a>. These increasingly amalgamated bodies later known collectively as the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a> have grown since, along with their legal successor, the EU, both in size through <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">accessions of further 21 states</a> as well as in power through acquisitions of various policy areas to their remit by the virtue of the abovementioned treaties, as well as numerous other ones, such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modified_Brussels_Treaty" title="Modified Brussels Treaty">Modified Brussels Treaty</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Merger_Treaty" title="Merger Treaty">Merger Treaty</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Single_European_Act" title="Single European Act">Single European Act</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Amsterdam" title="Treaty of Amsterdam">Treaty of Amsterdam</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Nice" title="Treaty of Nice">Treaty of Nice</a>. In 2012, the EU was awarded the <a href="/wiki/2012_Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="2012 Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although the United Kingdom became in <a href="/wiki/2020" title="2020">2020</a> the only member state to <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">leave the EU</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[23]</a></sup>  several further countries are <a href="/wiki/Potential_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Potential enlargement of the European Union">aspiring or negotiating to join it</a>. 
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_European_Union" title="History of the European Union">History of the European Union</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a chronological guide, see <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_European_Union_history" title="Timeline of European Union history">Timeline of European Union history</a>.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">Treaties of the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ideas_of_European_unity_before_1948" title="Ideas of European unity before 1948">Ideas of European unity before 1948</a> and <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Dunkirk" title="Treaty of Dunkirk">Treaty of Dunkirk</a></div>
<p>After the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a>, but particularly with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internationalism_(politics)" title="Internationalism (politics)">internationalism</a> was gaining, with the creation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bretton_Woods_System" title="Bretton Woods System">Bretton Woods System</a> in 1944, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in 1945 and the <a href="/wiki/French_Union" title="French Union">French Union</a> (1946‍–‍1958), the latter directing <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">decolonization</a> by possibly integrating its colonies into a European community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-27">[24]</a></sup> In this light <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a> was seen, already during the war, as an antidote to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extreme_nationalism" title="Extreme nationalism">extreme nationalism</a> which had devastated parts of the continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ventotene_Manifesto" title="Ventotene Manifesto">Ventotene prison Manifesto</a> of 1941 by <a href="/wiki/Altiero_Spinelli" title="Altiero Spinelli">Altiero Spinelli</a> propagated European integration through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Resistance" title="Italian Resistance">Italian Resistance</a> and after 1943 through the <a href="/wiki/European_Federalist_Movement" title="European Federalist Movement">European Federalist Movement</a>. <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> called in 1943 for a post-war "Council of Europe"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[27]</a></sup> and on 19 September 1946, at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_of_Z%C3%BCrich" title="University of Zürich">University of Zürich</a>, coincidentally<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Union_of_European_Federalists_(UEF)_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Union_of_European_Federalists_(UEF)-31">[28]</a></sup> parallel to the <a href="/wiki/Hertensteiner_Cross" title="Hertensteiner Cross">Hertenstein Congress</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_European_Federalists" title="Union of European Federalists">Union of European Federalists</a>, for a <a href="/wiki/United_States_of_Europe" title="United States of Europe">United States of Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[29]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_von_Coudenhove-Kalergi" title="Richard von Coudenhove-Kalergi">Richard von Coudenhove-Kalergi</a>, who successfully established during the <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">interwar period</a> the oldest organization for European integration, the <a href="/wiki/Paneuropean_Union" title="Paneuropean Union">Paneuropean Union</a>, founded in June 1947 the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliamentary_Union" title="European Parliamentary Union">European Parliamentary Union</a> (EPU).
</p><p>Towards the end of World War II, the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">There Allied Powers</a> discussed during the <a href="/wiki/Tehran_Conference" title="Tehran Conference">Tehran Conference</a> and the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Conference_(1943)" title="Moscow Conference (1943)">1943 Moscow Conference</a> the plans to establish joint institutions. This led to a decision at the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a> in 1944 to include Free France as the Fourth Allied Power and to form a <a href="/wiki/European_Advisory_Commission" title="European Advisory Commission">European Advisory Commission</a>, later replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Foreign_Ministers" title="Council of Foreign Ministers">Council of Foreign Ministers</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Allied_Control_Council" title="Allied Control Council">Allied Control Council</a>, following the German surrender and the <a href="/wiki/Potsdam_Agreement" title="Potsdam Agreement">Potsdam Agreement</a> in <a href="/wiki/1945" title="1945">1945</a>.
</p><p>The growing rift among the Four Powers became evident as a result of the rigged <a href="/wiki/1947_Polish_legislative_election" title="1947 Polish legislative election">1947 Polish legislative election</a> which constituted an open breach of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yalta_Agreement" title="Yalta Agreement">Yalta Agreement</a>, followed by the announcement of the <a href="/wiki/Truman_Doctrine" title="Truman Doctrine">Truman Doctrine</a> on 12 March 1947. On 4 March 1947 France and the United Kingdom signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Dunkirk" title="Treaty of Dunkirk">Treaty of Dunkirk</a> for mutual assistance in the event of future military aggression in the aftermath of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> against any of the pair. The rationale for the treaty was the threat of a potential future military attack, specifically a Soviet one in practice, though publicised under the disguise of a German one, according to the official statements. Immediately following the <a href="/wiki/1948_Czechoslovak_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1948 Czechoslovak coup d'état">February 1948 coup d'état</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Communist Party of Czechoslovakia">Communist Party of Czechoslovakia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/London_Six-Power_Conference" title="London Six-Power Conference">London Six-Power Conference</a> was held, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> boycott of the Allied Control Council and its incapacitation, an event marking the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. The remainder of the year 1948 marked the beginning of the institutionalised modern European integration.
</p>
<h3><span id="Initial_years_and_the_Paris_Treaty_.281948.E2.80.8D.E2.80.93.E2.80.8D1957.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_years_and_the_Paris_Treaty_(1948‍–‍1957)">Initial years and the Paris Treaty (1948‍–‍1957)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Europa_Congres_Ridderzaal_Den_Haag._Overzicht,_Bestanddeelnr_902-7379.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2854" data-file-width="3397" decoding="async" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Europa_Congres_Ridderzaal_Den_Haag._Overzicht%2C_Bestanddeelnr_902-7379.jpg/220px-Europa_Congres_Ridderzaal_Den_Haag._Overzicht%2C_Bestanddeelnr_902-7379.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Europa_Congres_Ridderzaal_Den_Haag._Overzicht%2C_Bestanddeelnr_902-7379.jpg/330px-Europa_Congres_Ridderzaal_Den_Haag._Overzicht%2C_Bestanddeelnr_902-7379.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Europa_Congres_Ridderzaal_Den_Haag._Overzicht%2C_Bestanddeelnr_902-7379.jpg/440px-Europa_Congres_Ridderzaal_Den_Haag._Overzicht%2C_Bestanddeelnr_902-7379.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Europa_Congres_Ridderzaal_Den_Haag._Overzicht,_Bestanddeelnr_902-7379.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Meeting in the <a href="/wiki/Ridderzaal" title="Ridderzaal">Hall of Knights</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>, during the congress (9 May 1948)</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_European_integration_(1948%E2%80%931957)" title="History of the European integration (1948–1957)">History of the European integration (1948–1957)</a></div>
<p>The year 1948 marked the beginning of the institutionalised modern <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a>. In March 1948 the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brussels" title="Treaty of Brussels">Treaty of Brussels</a> was signed, establishing the <a href="/wiki/Western_Union_(alliance)" title="Western Union (alliance)">Western Union</a> (WU), followed by the <a href="/wiki/International_Authority_for_the_Ruhr" title="International Authority for the Ruhr">International Authority for the Ruhr</a>. Furthermore, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organization_for_European_Economic_Co-operation" title="Organization for European Economic Co-operation">Organization for European Economic Co-operation</a>, the predecessor of the OECD, was also founded in 1948 to manage the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a>, triggering as a Soviet response formation of the <a href="/wiki/Comecon" title="Comecon">Comecon</a>. The ensuing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hague_Congress_(1948)" title="Hague Congress (1948)">Hague Congress</a> of May 1948 was a pivotal moment in European integration, as it led to the creation of the <a href="/wiki/European_Movement_International" title="European Movement International">European Movement International</a>, the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Europe" title="College of Europe">College of Europe</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[30]</a></sup> and most importantly to the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> on 5 May 1949 (today its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Europe_day" title="Europe day">Europe day</a>). The Council of Europe was one of the first institutions to bring the sovereign nations of (then only Western) Europe together, raising great hopes and fevered debates in the following two years for further European integration.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It has since been a broad forum to further cooperation and shared issues, achieving for example the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a> in 1950. Essential for the actual birth of the institutions of the EU was the <a href="/wiki/Schuman_Declaration" title="Schuman Declaration">Schuman Declaration</a> on 9 May 1950 (the day after the fifth <a href="/wiki/Victory_in_Europe_Day" title="Victory in Europe Day">Victory in Europe Day</a>) and the decision by six nations (France, Belgium, Netherlands, Luxembourg, West Germany and Italy) to follow <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schuman" title="Schuman">Schuman</a> and draft the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1951)" title="Treaty of Paris (1951)">Treaty of Paris</a>. This treaty created in 1952 the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a> (ECSC), which was built on the <a href="/wiki/International_Authority_for_the_Ruhr" title="International Authority for the Ruhr">International Authority for the Ruhr</a>, installed by the Western Allies in 1949 to regulate the coal and steel industries of the Ruhr area in West Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[31]</a></sup> Backed by the <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a> with large funds coming from the United States since 1948, the ECSC became a milestone organization, enabling European economic development and integration and being the origin of the main institutions of the EU such as the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">Parliament</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[32]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Founding_fathers_of_the_European_Union" title="Founding fathers of the European Union">Founding fathers of the European Union</a> understood that coal and steel were the two industries essential for waging war, and believed that by tying their national industries together, a future war between their nations became much less likely.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_History_45-59_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_45-59-36">[33]</a></sup>
In parallel with Schuman, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pleven_Plan" title="Pleven Plan">Pleven Plan</a> of 1951 tried but failed to tie the institutions of the developing European community under the <a href="/wiki/European_Political_Community_(1952)" title="European Political Community (1952)">European Political Community</a>, which was to include the also proposed <a href="/wiki/Treaty_establishing_the_European_Defence_Community" title="Treaty establishing the European Defence Community">European Defence Community</a>, an alternative to <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> joining <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> which was established in 1949 under the <a href="/wiki/Truman_Doctrine" title="Truman Doctrine">Truman Doctrine</a>. In 1954 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modified_Brussels_Treaty" title="Modified Brussels Treaty">Modified Brussels Treaty</a> transformed the Western Union into the <a href="/wiki/Western_European_Union" title="Western European Union">Western European Union</a> (WEU). West Germany eventually joined in 1955 both WEU and NATO, prompting the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> to form the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> in 1955 as an institutional framework for its military dominatin in the countries of <a href="/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe" title="Central and Eastern Europe">Central and Eastern Europe</a>. Assessing the progress of European integration the <a href="/wiki/Messina_Conference" title="Messina Conference">Messina Conference</a> was held in 1955, ordering the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spaak_report" title="Spaak report">Spaak report</a>, which in 1956 recommended the next significant steps of European integration.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Treaty_of_Rome_.281957.E2.80.8D.E2.80.93.E2.80.8D1992.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Treaty_of_Rome_(1957‍–‍1992)">Treaty of Rome (1957‍–‍1992)</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_European_Communities_(1958%E2%80%931972)" title="History of the European Communities (1958–1972)">History of the European Communities (1958–1972)</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_European_Communities_(1973%E2%80%931993)" title="History of the European Communities (1973–1993)">History of the European Communities (1973–1993)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="680" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif/220px-EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif/330px-EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif/440px-EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EC-EU-enlargement_animation.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The continental territories of the member states of the European Union (European Communities pre-1993), coloured in order of accession</div></div></div>
<p>In 1957, Belgium, France, Italy, Luxembourg, the Netherlands, and West Germany signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">Treaty of Rome</a>, which created the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC) and established a <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">customs union</a>. They also signed another pact creating the <a href="/wiki/European_Atomic_Energy_Community" title="European Atomic Energy Community">European Atomic Energy Community</a> (Euratom) for co-operation in developing <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">nuclear power</a>. Both treaties came into force in 1958.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_History_45-59_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_45-59-36">[33]</a></sup>
</p><p>The EEC and Euratom were created separately from the ECSC and they shared the same courts and the Common Assembly. The EEC was headed by <a href="/wiki/Walter_Hallstein" title="Walter Hallstein">Walter Hallstein</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hallstein_Commission" title="Hallstein Commission">Hallstein Commission</a>) and Euratom was headed by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Armand" title="Louis Armand">Louis Armand</a> (<a href="/wiki/Armand_Commission" title="Armand Commission">Armand Commission</a>) and then <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_Hirsch" title="Étienne Hirsch">Étienne Hirsch</a>. Euratom was to integrate sectors in nuclear power while the EEC would develop a customs union among members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[35]</a></sup> The OEEC was in turn reformed in 1961 into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> and its membership was extended to non-European states, the US and Canada.
</p><p>During the 1960s, tensions began to show, with France seeking to limit supranational power. Nevertheless, in 1965 an agreement was reached, and on 1 July 1967 the <a href="/wiki/Merger_Treaty" title="Merger Treaty">Merger Treaty</a> created a single set of institutions for the three communities, which were collectively referred to as the <i><a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENA_Merge_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_Merge-39">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jean_Rey_(politician)" title="Jean Rey (politician)">Jean Rey</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">presided over</a> the first merged commission (<a href="/wiki/Rey_Commission" title="Rey Commission">Rey Commission</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[38]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1973, the communities were enlarged to include Denmark (including <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, which later <a href="/wiki/1982_Greenlandic_European_Communities_membership_referendum" title="1982 Greenlandic European Communities membership referendum">left the Communities</a> in 1985, following a dispute over fishing rights), Ireland, and the <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_the_United_Kingdom_to_the_European_Communities" title="Accession of the United Kingdom to the European Communities">United Kingdom</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENA_First_enlargement_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_First_enlargement-42">[39]</a></sup> Norway had negotiated to join at the same time, but Norwegian voters rejected membership in a <a href="/wiki/1972_Norwegian_European_Communities_membership_referendum" title="1972 Norwegian European Communities membership referendum">referendum</a>. In 1979, the <a href="/wiki/1979_European_Parliament_election" title="1979 European Parliament election">first direct elections</a> to the European Parliament were held.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENA_New_Parliament_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_New_Parliament-43">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>Greece joined in 1981, Portugal and Spain following in 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ENA_Enlargement_negotiations_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-ENA_Enlargement_negotiations-44">[41]</a></sup> In 1985, the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a> paved the way for the creation of open borders without passport controls between most member states and some non-member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[42]</a></sup> In 1986, the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Europe" title="Flag of Europe">European flag</a> began to be used by the EEC<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[43]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Single_European_Act" title="Single European Act">Single European Act</a> was signed.
</p><p>In 1990, after <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">the fall of the Eastern Bloc</a>, the former <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a> became part of the communities as part of a <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">reunified Germany</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_History_80-89_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_80-89-47">[44]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span id="Maastricht.2C_Amsterdam_and_Nice_treaties_.281993.E2.80.8D.E2.80.93.E2.80.8D2004.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Maastricht,_Amsterdam_and_Nice_treaties_(1993‍–‍2004)">Maastricht, Amsterdam and Nice treaties (1993‍–‍2004)</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_European_Union_(1993%E2%80%932004)" title="History of the European Union (1993–2004)">History of the European Union (1993–2004)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GER_%E2%80%94_BY_%E2%80%94_Regensburg_-_Donaumarkt_1_(Museum_der_Bayerischen_Geschichte;_Vertrag_von_Maastricht)_(cropped).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1817" data-file-width="3621" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/GER_%E2%80%94_BY_%E2%80%94_Regensburg_-_Donaumarkt_1_%28Museum_der_Bayerischen_Geschichte%3B_Vertrag_von_Maastricht%29_%28cropped%29.JPG/220px-GER_%E2%80%94_BY_%E2%80%94_Regensburg_-_Donaumarkt_1_%28Museum_der_Bayerischen_Geschichte%3B_Vertrag_von_Maastricht%29_%28cropped%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/GER_%E2%80%94_BY_%E2%80%94_Regensburg_-_Donaumarkt_1_%28Museum_der_Bayerischen_Geschichte%3B_Vertrag_von_Maastricht%29_%28cropped%29.JPG/330px-GER_%E2%80%94_BY_%E2%80%94_Regensburg_-_Donaumarkt_1_%28Museum_der_Bayerischen_Geschichte%3B_Vertrag_von_Maastricht%29_%28cropped%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/GER_%E2%80%94_BY_%E2%80%94_Regensburg_-_Donaumarkt_1_%28Museum_der_Bayerischen_Geschichte%3B_Vertrag_von_Maastricht%29_%28cropped%29.JPG/440px-GER_%E2%80%94_BY_%E2%80%94_Regensburg_-_Donaumarkt_1_%28Museum_der_Bayerischen_Geschichte%3B_Vertrag_von_Maastricht%29_%28cropped%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GER_%E2%80%94_BY_%E2%80%94_Regensburg_-_Donaumarkt_1_(Museum_der_Bayerischen_Geschichte;_Vertrag_von_Maastricht)_(cropped).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Treaty of Maastricht, shown containing the signatures of some ministers representing their heads of state</div></div></div>
<p>The European Union was formally established when the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a>—whose main architects were <a href="/wiki/Horst_K%C3%B6hler" title="Horst Köhler">Horst Köhler</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[45]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Helmut_Kohl" title="Helmut Kohl">Helmut Kohl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Mitterrand" title="François Mitterrand">François Mitterrand</a>—came into force on 1 November 1993.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECraigDe_Burca201115_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECraigDe_Burca201115-24">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[46]</a></sup> The treaty also gave the name <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Community" title="European Community">European Community</a></i> to the EEC, even if it was referred to as such before the treaty. With further enlargement planned to include the former <a href="/wiki/Communist_state" title="Communist state">communist states</a> of Central and Eastern Europe, as well as <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_criteria" title="Copenhagen criteria">Copenhagen criteria</a> for candidate members to join the EU were agreed upon in June 1993. The expansion of the EU introduced a new level of complexity and discord.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-50">[47]</a></sup> In 1995, Austria, Finland, and Sweden <a href="/wiki/1995_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="1995 enlargement of the European Union">joined</a> the EU.
</p><p>In 2002, euro banknotes and coins replaced national currencies in 12 of the member states. Since then, the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> has increased to encompass 19 countries. The euro currency became the second-largest reserve currency in the world. In 2004, the EU saw <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">its biggest enlargement to date</a> when Cyprus, the Czech Republic, Estonia, Hungary, Latvia, Lithuania, Malta, Poland, Slovakia, and Slovenia joined the union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_History_00_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_00-51">[48]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Consolidation.2C_the_Treaty_of_Lisbon_and_Brexit_.282004.E2.80.8D.E2.80.93.E2.80.8Dpresent.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Consolidation,_the_Treaty_of_Lisbon_and_Brexit_(2004‍–‍present)">Consolidation, the Treaty of Lisbon and Brexit (2004‍–‍present)</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_European_Union_(2004%E2%80%93present)" title="History of the European Union (2004–present)">History of the European Union (2004–present)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(04).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="466" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%2804%29.jpg/220px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%2804%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%2804%29.jpg/330px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%2804%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%2804%29.jpg/440px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%2804%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(04).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Signing_of_the_Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Signing of the Treaty of Lisbon">Signing</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Jer%C3%B3nimos_Monastery" title="Jerónimos Monastery">Jerónimos Monastery</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, Portugal</div></div></div>
<p>In 2007, Bulgaria and Romania became EU members. Later that year, Slovenia adopted the euro,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_History_00_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_00-51">[48]</a></sup> followed by Cyprus and Malta in 2008, Slovakia in 2009, Estonia in 2011, Latvia in 2014, and Lithuania in 2015.
</p><p>On 1 December 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Lisbon Treaty</a> entered into force and reformed many aspects of the EU. In particular, it changed the legal structure of the European Union, merging the <a href="/wiki/Three_pillars_of_the_European_Union" title="Three pillars of the European Union">EU three pillars</a> system into a single legal entity provisioned with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legal_personality" title="Legal personality">legal personality</a>, created a permanent <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">president of the European Council</a>, the first of which was <a href="/wiki/Herman_Van_Rompuy" title="Herman Van Rompuy">Herman Van Rompuy</a>, and strengthened the position of the <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy" title="High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy">high representative of the union for foreign affairs and security policy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPiris2010448_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPiris2010448-52">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, the EU received the <a href="/wiki/2012_Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="2012 Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> for having "contributed to the advancement of peace and reconciliation, democracy, and human rights in Europe".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup> In 2013, <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> became the 28th EU member.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>From the beginning of the 2010s, the cohesion of the European Union has been tested by several issues, including <a href="/wiki/European_debt_crisis" title="European debt crisis">a debt crisis in some of the Eurozone countries</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_migrant_crisis" title="European migrant crisis">increasing migration from Africa and Asia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">United Kingdom's withdrawal from the EU</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCUKREFRESLT_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBCUKREFRESLT-57">[54]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum">referendum in the UK on its membership of the European Union</a> was held in 2016, with 51.9 per cent of participants voting to leave.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTEUBrexit_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTEUBrexit-58">[55]</a></sup> The UK formally notified the European Council of its decision to leave on 29 March 2017, initiating the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Article_50_of_the_Treaty_on_European_Union" title="Article 50 of the Treaty on European Union">formal withdrawal procedure for leaving the EU</a>; following extensions to the process, the UK left the European Union on 31 January 2020, though most areas of EU law continued to apply to the UK for a transition period which lasted until 23:00 GMT on 31 December 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[56]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_demographics">Geography and demographics</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_European_Union" title="Geography of the European Union">Geography of the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_European_Union" title="Demographics of the European Union">Demographics of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:European_Union_relief_laea_location_map.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1198" data-file-width="1401" decoding="async" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/European_Union_relief_laea_location_map.svg/260px-European_Union_relief_laea_location_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/European_Union_relief_laea_location_map.svg/390px-European_Union_relief_laea_location_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/European_Union_relief_laea_location_map.svg/520px-European_Union_relief_laea_location_map.svg.png 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:European_Union_relief_laea_location_map.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Topographic map of the European Union</div></div></div>

Islands">Ionian Islands</a> of Greece</div></div></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_geography">Physical geography</span></h3>
<p>The European Union's member states cover an area of 4,233,262 square kilometres (1,634,472 sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Area.and.population.figure_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Area.and.population.figure-60">[d]</a></sup> The EU's highest peak is <a href="/wiki/Mont_Blanc" title="Mont Blanc">Mont Blanc</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Graian_Alps" title="Graian Alps">Graian Alps</a>, 4,810.45 metres (15,782 ft) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[57]</a></sup> The lowest points in the EU are <a href="/wiki/Lammefjorden" title="Lammefjorden">Lammefjorden</a>, Denmark, and <a href="/wiki/Zuidplaspolder" title="Zuidplaspolder">Zuidplaspolder</a>, Netherlands, at 7 m (23 ft) below sea level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[58]</a></sup> The landscape, climate, and economy of the EU are influenced by its coastline, which is 65,993 kilometres (41,006 mi) long.
</p><p>Including the overseas territories of France which are located outside the continent of Europe, but which are members of the union, the EU experiences most <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">types of climate</a> from <a href="/wiki/Polar_climate" title="Polar climate">Arctic</a> (north-east Europe) to tropical (<a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>), rendering meteorological averages for the EU as a whole meaningless. The majority of the population lives in areas with a temperate <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">maritime climate</a> (North-Western Europe and Central Europe), a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (Southern Europe), or a warm summer continental or <a href="/wiki/Hemiboreal" title="Hemiboreal">hemiboreal</a> climate (Central Europe and Southeastern Europe).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Humid_Continental_climate_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Humid_Continental_climate-63">[59]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EU_27_(from_2020)_population_pyramid_in_2021.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2878" data-file-width="3610" decoding="async" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/EU_27_%28from_2020%29_population_pyramid_in_2021.svg/220px-EU_27_%28from_2020%29_population_pyramid_in_2021.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/EU_27_%28from_2020%29_population_pyramid_in_2021.svg/330px-EU_27_%28from_2020%29_population_pyramid_in_2021.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/EU_27_%28from_2020%29_population_pyramid_in_2021.svg/440px-EU_27_%28from_2020%29_population_pyramid_in_2021.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EU_27_(from_2020)_population_pyramid_in_2021.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population pyramid of the EU 27 (from 2020) in 2021</div></div></div>
<p>On 1 January 2021, the population of the European Union was about 447 million people (5.8 per cent of the world population).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-population-64">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[61]</a></sup> In 2015, 5.1<span class="nowrap"> </span>million children were born in the EU-28 corresponding to a birth rate of 10 per 1,000, which is 8 births below the world average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[62]</a></sup> For comparison, the EU-28 birth rate had stood at 10.6 in 2000, 12.8 in 1985 and 16.3 in 1970.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[63]</a></sup> Its population growth rate was positive at an estimated 0.23 per cent in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, 47.3<span class="nowrap"> </span>million people who lived in the EU were born outside their resident country. This corresponds to 9.4 per cent of the total EU population. Of these, 31.4<span class="nowrap"> </span>million (6.3 per cent) were born outside the EU and 16.0<span class="nowrap"> </span>million (3.2 per cent) were born in another EU member state. The largest absolute numbers of people born outside the EU were in Germany (6.4<span class="nowrap"> </span>million), France (5.1<span class="nowrap"> </span>million), the United Kingdom (4.7<span class="nowrap"> </span>million), Spain (4.1<span class="nowrap"> </span>million), Italy (3.2<span class="nowrap"> </span>million), and the Netherlands (1.4<span class="nowrap"> </span>million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[65]</a></sup> In 2017, approximately 825,000 people acquired <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_European_Union" title="Citizenship of the European Union">citizenship</a> of a member state of the European Union. The <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Europe" title="Immigration to Europe">largest groups</a> were nationals of Morocco, Albania, India, Turkey, and Pakistan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[66]</a></sup> 2.4<span class="nowrap"> </span>million <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Europe" title="Immigration to Europe">immigrants</a> from non-EU countries entered the EU in 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanisation">Urbanisation</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_the_European_Union_by_population_within_city_limits" title="List of cities in the European Union by population within city limits">List of cities in the European Union by population within city limits</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_in_the_European_Union" title="List of urban areas in the European Union">list of urban areas in the European Union</a></div>
<p>The EU's population is highly urbanised: some 75 per cent of inhabitants lived in <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban areas</a> in 2006. Cities are largely spread out across the EU with a large grouping in and around the <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[69]</a></sup> The EU contains about 40 urban areas with populations of over 1<span class="nowrap"> </span>million. With a population of over 13 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-paris_AAV20_pop_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-paris_AAV20_pop-74">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> is the largest metropolitan area and the only <a href="/wiki/Megacity" title="Megacity">megacity</a> in the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eurostat_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-eurostat-75">[71]</a></sup> Paris is followed by <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ruhr" title="Ruhr">Ruhr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, all with a metropolitan population of over 4<span class="nowrap"> </span>million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-appsso.eurostat.ec.europa.eu_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-appsso.eurostat.ec.europa.eu-76">[72]</a></sup>
</p><p>The EU also has numerous <a href="/wiki/Conurbation" title="Conurbation">polycentric</a> urbanised regions like <a href="/wiki/Rhine-Ruhr" title="Rhine-Ruhr">Rhine-Ruhr</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">Cologne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dortmund" title="Dortmund">Dortmund</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf" title="Düsseldorf">Düsseldorf</a> et al.), <a href="/wiki/Randstad" title="Randstad">Randstad</a> (<a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utrecht" title="Utrecht">Utrecht</a> et al.), <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Rhine-Main" title="Frankfurt Rhine-Main">Frankfurt Rhine-Main</a> (<a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wiesbaden" title="Wiesbaden">Wiesbaden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mainz" title="Mainz">Mainz</a> et al.), the <a href="/wiki/Flemish_Diamond" title="Flemish Diamond">Flemish Diamond</a> (<a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leuven" title="Leuven">Leuven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghent" title="Ghent">Ghent</a> et al.) and <a href="/wiki/Upper_Silesian_metropolitan_area" title="Upper Silesian metropolitan area">Upper Silesian area</a> (<a href="/wiki/Katowice" title="Katowice">Katowice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ostrava" title="Ostrava">Ostrava</a> et al.).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eurostat_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-eurostat-75">[71]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>

<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>
</th>
<td>&lt;1%
</td>
<td>&lt;1%
</td></tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a>
</th>
<td>&lt;1%
</td>
<td>&lt;1%
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The European Union has 24 official languages: <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_language" title="Bulgarian language">Bulgarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croatian_language" title="Croatian language">Croatian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovene_language" title="Slovene language">Slovene</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>. Important documents, such as legislation, are translated into every official language and the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> provides translation for documents and plenary sessions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Official_Languages_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Official_Languages-85">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[79]</a></sup> In 2020, the EU stated that translation and interpreting costs were less than 1% of its annual budget of €148 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[80]</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to the high number of official languages, most of the institutions use only a handful of working languages. The European Commission conducts its internal business in three <i>procedural languages</i>: English, French, and German<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-procedural_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-procedural-88">[81]</a></sup> Similarly, the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Justice_of_the_European_Union" title="Court of Justice of the European Union">Court of Justice of the European Union</a> uses French as the working language,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[82]</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a> conducts its business primarily in English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[84]</a></sup>
</p><p>Even though <a href="/wiki/Language_policy" title="Language policy">language policy</a> is the responsibility of member states, EU institutions promote multilingualism among its citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[h]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[85]</a></sup> In 2012, English was the most widely spoken language in the EU, being understood by 51 per cent of the EU population when counting both native and non-native speakers. However, following the UK's exit from the bloc in early 2020, the percentage of the EU population who spoke English as their native language fell from 13 per cent to 1 per cent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[86]</a></sup> German is the most widely spoken mother tongue (18 per cent of the EU population), and the second most widely understood foreign language, followed by French (13 per cent of the EU population). In addition, both are official languages of several EU member states. More than half (56 per cent) of EU citizens are able to engage in a conversation in a language other than their mother tongue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eurobarometer_Languages_P3_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eurobarometer_Languages_P3-95">[87]</a></sup>
</p><p>A total of twenty official languages of the EU belong to the <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European</a> <a href="/wiki/Language_family" title="Language family">language family</a>, represented by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balto-Slavic" title="Balto-Slavic">Balto-Slavic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[i]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Italic_languages" title="Italic languages">Italic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[j]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germanic_Europe" title="Germanic Europe">Germanic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[k]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Hellenic_languages" title="Hellenic languages">Hellenic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[l]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_languages" title="Celtic languages">Celtic</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[m]</a></sup> branches. Only four languages, namely <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estonian_language" title="Estonian language">Estonian</a> (all three <a href="/wiki/Uralic_languages" title="Uralic languages">Uralic</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a> (<a href="/wiki/Semitic_languages" title="Semitic languages">Semitic</a>), are not Indo-European languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Many_tongues,_one_family_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Many_tongues,_one_family-101">[88]</a></sup> The three official alphabets of the European Union (<a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">Cyrillic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greek_alphabet" title="Greek alphabet">modern Greek</a>) all derive from the <a href="/wiki/Archaic_Greek_alphabets" title="Archaic Greek alphabets">Archaic Greek scripts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-102">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[90]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Luxembourgish" title="Luxembourgish">Luxembourgish</a> (in Luxembourg) and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a> (in Cyprus) are the only two national languages that are not official languages of the EU. On 26 February 2016, it was made public that Cyprus has asked to make Turkish an official EU language, in a "gesture" that could help solve the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyprus_dispute" title="Cyprus dispute">division of the country</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>Besides the 24 official languages, there are about 150 <a href="/wiki/Regional_language" title="Regional language">regional</a> and <a href="/wiki/Minority_language" title="Minority language">minority languages</a>, spoken by up to 50 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Many_tongues,_one_family_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-Many_tongues,_one_family-101">[88]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galician</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> are not recognised official languages of the European Union but have official status in one member state (Spain): therefore, official translations of the treaties are made into them and citizens have the right to correspond with the institutions in these languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-105">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[93]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_for_Regional_or_Minority_Languages" title="European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages">European Charter for Regional or Minority Languages</a> ratified by most EU states provides general guidelines that states can follow to protect their linguistic heritage. The <a href="/wiki/European_Day_of_Languages" title="European Day of Languages">European Day of Languages</a> is held annually on 26 September and is aimed at encouraging language learning across Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[94]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_European_Union" title="Religion in the European Union">Religion in the European Union</a></div>
<table class="wikitable sortable mw-collapsible plainrowheaders floatright" style="font-size: 90%;">

<td style="text-align: right;">10.4

</td></tr>

<p>The EU has no formal connection to any religion. Article 17 of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Functioning_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union">Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[95]</a></sup> recognises the "status under national law of churches and religious associations" as well as that of "philosophical and non-confessional organisations".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Consolidated_Treaties_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Consolidated_Treaties-109">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>The preamble to the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Treaty on European Union</a> mentions the "cultural, religious and humanist inheritance of Europe".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Consolidated_Treaties_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-Consolidated_Treaties-109">[96]</a></sup> Discussion over the draft texts of the European Constitution and later the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a> included proposals to mention <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> or a <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">god</a>, or both, in the preamble of the text, but the idea faced opposition and was dropped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUO_Merkel_God_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-EUO_Merkel_God-110">[97]</a></sup>
</p><p>Christians in the European Union are divided among members of Catholicism (both <a href="/wiki/Latin_Church" title="Latin Church">Roman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholic_Churches" title="Eastern Catholic Churches">Eastern Rite</a>), numerous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> denominations (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglicans" title="Anglicans">Anglicans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutherans" title="Lutherans">Lutherans</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reformed_tradition" title="Reformed tradition">Reformed</a> forming the bulk of this category), and the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a>. In 2009, the EU had an estimated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Muslim_population" title="List of countries by Muslim population">Muslim population</a> of 13 million,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mgmpPRC_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-mgmpPRC-111">[98]</a></sup> and an estimated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_population" title="Jewish population">Jewish population</a> of over a million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[99]</a></sup> The other world religions of <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a> are also represented in the EU population.
</p><p>According to new polls about religiosity in the European Union in 2015 by <a href="/wiki/Eurobarometer" title="Eurobarometer">Eurobarometer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> is the largest religion in the European Union, accounting for 71.6 per cent of the EU population. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholics" title="Catholics">Catholics</a> are the largest Christian group, accounting for 45.3 per cent of the EU population, while <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestants</a> make up 11.1 per cent, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox</a> make up 9.6 per cent, and other Christians make up 5.6 per cent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EB2015_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-EB2015-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Eurobarometer" title="Eurobarometer">Eurobarometer</a> opinion polls showed in 2005 that 52 per cent of EU citizens believed in a god, 27 per cent in "some sort of spirit or life force", and 18 per cent had no form of belief.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eurostat_Religion_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat_Religion-113">[100]</a></sup> Many countries have experienced falling church attendance and membership in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-About_SecE_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-About_SecE-114">[101]</a></sup> The countries where the fewest people reported a religious belief were Estonia (16 per cent) and the Czech Republic (19 per cent).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eurostat_Religion_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat_Religion-113">[100]</a></sup> The most religious countries were Malta (95 per cent, predominantly Catholic) as well as Cyprus and Romania (both predominantly Orthodox) each with about 90 per cent of citizens professing a belief in God. Across the EU, belief was higher among women, older people, those with religious upbringing, those who left school at 15 or 16, and those "positioning themselves on the right of the political scale".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eurostat_Religion_113-2"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat_Religion-113">[100]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Europe" title="Healthcare in Europe">Healthcare in Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Health_Threat_Unit" title="Health Threat Unit">Health Threat Unit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rapid_Alert_System_for_Food_and_Feed" title="Rapid Alert System for Food and Feed">Rapid Alert System for Food and Feed</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TRACES" title="TRACES">TRACES</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EUROPHYT" title="EUROPHYT">EUROPHYT</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EHIC_Slovenia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="269" data-file-width="414" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/EHIC_Slovenia.jpg/220px-EHIC_Slovenia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/EHIC_Slovenia.jpg/330px-EHIC_Slovenia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ad/EHIC_Slovenia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EHIC_Slovenia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/European_Health_Insurance_Card" title="European Health Insurance Card">European Health Insurance Card</a> (Slovenian version pictured)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TetrapackMilk.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="311" data-file-width="824" decoding="async" height="83" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/TetrapackMilk.jpg/220px-TetrapackMilk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/TetrapackMilk.jpg/330px-TetrapackMilk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/TetrapackMilk.jpg/440px-TetrapackMilk.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TetrapackMilk.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/EC_identification_and_health_marks" title="EC identification and health marks">EU identification marks</a> on a German <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tetrapak" title="Tetrapak">Tetrapak</a> milk container</div></div></div>
<p>The Article 35 of the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights_of_the_European_Union" title="Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union">Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union</a> affirms that "A high level of human health protection shall be ensured in the definition and implementation of all Union policies and activities". The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Directorate-General_for_Health_and_Consumers_(European_Commission)" title="Directorate-General for Health and Consumers (European Commission)">Directorate-General for Health and Consumers</a> seeks to align national laws on the protection of people's health, on the consumers' rights, on the safety of food and other products.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[102]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>All EU and many other European countries offer their citizens a free <a href="/wiki/European_Health_Insurance_Card" title="European Health Insurance Card">European Health Insurance Card</a> which, on a reciprocal basis, provides insurance for emergency medical treatment insurance when visiting other participating European countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[105]</a></sup> A directive on cross-border healthcare aims at promoting co-operation on health care between member states and facilitating access to safe and high-quality cross-border healthcare for European patients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p>The EU has some of the highest levels of life expectancy in the world, with Spain, Italy, Sweden, France, Malta, Ireland, Netherlands, Luxembourg, and Greece all among the world's top 20 countries with the highest life expectancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hdr-life-exp_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-hdr-life-exp-122">[109]</a></sup> In general, life expectancy is lower in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> than in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[110]</a></sup> In 2018, the EU region with the highest life expectancy was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comunidad_de_Madrid" title="Comunidad de Madrid">Madrid</a>, Spain at 85.2 years, followed by the Spanish regions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Rioja_(Spain)" title="La Rioja (Spain)">La Rioja</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Castilla_y_Le%C3%B3n" title="Castilla y León">Castilla y León</a> both at 84.3 years, <a href="/wiki/Trentino" title="Trentino">Trentino</a> in Italy at 84.3 years and <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele-de-France" title="Île-de-France">Île-de-France</a> in France at 84.2 years. The overall life expectancy in the EU in 2018 was 81.0 years, higher than the World average of 72.6 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[111]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Member_states">Member states</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">Member state of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:552px;"><div class="noresize"><map name="ImageMap_425bd3d353257b07"><area alt="Croatia" coords="286,353,285,357,290,362,295,353,300,357,301,365,309,376,311,380,314,381,327,388,327,387,321,382,322,380,310,367,305,361,306,355,312,358,320,356,327,357,336,357,340,360,341,355,343,353,338,350,337,345,334,347,326,347,321,342,316,338,314,337,307,341,306,346,304,347,304,352,297,353,295,350,294,352,289,351,286,353"
