href="/wiki/File:Member_States_of_the_European_Union_(polar_stereographic_projection)_EN.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing the member states of the European Union (clickable)</div></div></div>
<p>Through successive <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">enlargements</a>, the European Union has grown from the <a href="/wiki/Inner_Six" title="Inner Six">six founding states</a> (Belgium, France, West Germany, Italy, Luxembourg, and the Netherlands) to 27 members. Countries accede to the union by becoming party to the founding <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">treaties</a>, thereby subjecting themselves to the privileges and obligations of EU membership. This entails a partial delegation of sovereignty to the institutions in return for representation within those institutions, a practice often referred to as "pooling of sovereignty".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[113]</a></sup>
</p><p>Several <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_the_European_Union" title="Special member state territories and the European Union">overseas territories</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">dependencies</a> of various member states are also formally part of the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[114]</a></sup>
</p><p>To become a member, a country must meet the <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_criteria" title="Copenhagen criteria">Copenhagen criteria</a>, defined at the 1993 meeting of the European Council in Copenhagen. These require a stable democracy that respects human rights and the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a>; a functioning <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>; and the acceptance of the obligations of membership, including EU law. Evaluation of a country's fulfilment of the criteria is the responsibility of the European Council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Accession_Criteria_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-Accession_Criteria-128">[115]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Article_50_of_the_Treaty_on_European_Union" title="Article 50 of the Treaty on European Union">Article 50</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Lisbon Treaty</a> provides the basis for a member to <a href="/wiki/Withdrawal_from_the_European_Union" title="Withdrawal from the European Union">leave the EU</a>. Two territories have left the union: <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> (an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autonomous_area" title="Autonomous area">autonomous province</a> of Denmark) withdrew in 1985;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[116]</a></sup> the United Kingdom formally invoked Article 50 of the Consolidated Treaty on European Union in 2017, and became the only sovereign state to leave when it <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">withdrew</a> from the EU in 2020.
</p><p>There are seven countries that are recognised as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Future_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Future enlargement of the European Union">candidates for membership</a>: <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Albania_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Albania to the European Union">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Moldova_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Moldova to the European Union">Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Montenegro_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Montenegro to the European Union">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_North_Macedonia_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of North Macedonia to the European Union">North Macedonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Serbia_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Serbia to the European Union">Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Turkey_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Turkey to the European Union">Turkey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Ukraine_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Ukraine to the European Union">Ukraine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Enlargement_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Enlargement-130">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[118]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Norway%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Norway–European Union relations">Norway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Switzerland–European Union relations">Switzerland</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accession_of_Iceland_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Iceland to the European Union">Iceland</a> have submitted membership applications in the past, but subsequently frozen or withdrawn them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-icelandover_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-icelandover-132">[119]</a></sup> Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Bosnia and Herzegovina to the European Union">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia%E2%80%93European_Union_relations#Proposed_European_Union_membership" title="Georgia–European Union relations">Georgia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Accession_of_Kosovo_to_the_European_Union" title="Accession of Kosovo to the European Union">Kosovo</a> are officially recognised as potential candidates,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Enlargement_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Enlargement-130">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[120]</a></sup> with Bosnia and Herzegovina and Georgia having submitted membership applications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[121]</a></sup>
</p><p>The four countries forming the <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">European Free Trade Association</a> (EFTA) are not EU members, but have partly committed to the EU's economy and regulations: Iceland, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a> and Norway, which are a part of the <a href="/wiki/Single_market" title="Single market">single market</a> through the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a>, and Switzerland, which has similar ties through <a href="/wiki/Switzerland%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Switzerland–European Union relations">bilateral treaties</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EEA_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-EEA-135">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CH_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-CH-136">[123]</a></sup> The relationships of the <a href="/wiki/Microstates_and_the_European_Union" title="Microstates and the European Union">European microstates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a> include the use of the euro and other areas of co-operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-euro_use_world_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-euro_use_world-137">[124]</a></sup>
</p>

<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span id="Politics.2C_law.2C_and_governance"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics,_law,_and_governance">Politics, law, and governance</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_European_Union" title="Politics of the European Union">Politics of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="744" data-file-width="1052" decoding="async" height="233" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg/330px-Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg/495px-Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg/660px-Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Organs_of_the_European_Union.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Organigram of the political system with the seven institutions of the Union in blue, national / intergovernmental elements in orange</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NextGenerationEU_-_StrongerTogether_-_Recovery_plan_for_Europe_-_Plan_de_relance_pour_l%27Europe_-_Heerstelplan_voor_Europe_-_Berlaymont.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="9024" data-file-width="12032" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/NextGenerationEU_-_StrongerTogether_-_Recovery_plan_for_Europe_-_Plan_de_relance_pour_l%27Europe_-_Heerstelplan_voor_Europe_-_Berlaymont.jpg/220px-NextGenerationEU_-_StrongerTogether_-_Recovery_plan_for_Europe_-_Plan_de_relance_pour_l%27Europe_-_Heerstelplan_voor_Europe_-_Berlaymont.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/NextGenerationEU_-_StrongerTogether_-_Recovery_plan_for_Europe_-_Plan_de_relance_pour_l%27Europe_-_Heerstelplan_voor_Europe_-_Berlaymont.jpg/330px-NextGenerationEU_-_StrongerTogether_-_Recovery_plan_for_Europe_-_Plan_de_relance_pour_l%27Europe_-_Heerstelplan_voor_Europe_-_Berlaymont.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/NextGenerationEU_-_StrongerTogether_-_Recovery_plan_for_Europe_-_Plan_de_relance_pour_l%27Europe_-_Heerstelplan_voor_Europe_-_Berlaymont.jpg/440px-NextGenerationEU_-_StrongerTogether_-_Recovery_plan_for_Europe_-_Plan_de_relance_pour_l%27Europe_-_Heerstelplan_voor_Europe_-_Berlaymont.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NextGenerationEU_-_StrongerTogether_-_Recovery_plan_for_Europe_-_Plan_de_relance_pour_l%27Europe_-_Heerstelplan_voor_Europe_-_Berlaymont.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Berlaymont_building" title="Berlaymont building">Berlaymont building</a> (<b><a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a></b>)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Europa_building_February_2016_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="510" data-file-width="699" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Europa_building_February_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Europa_building_February_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Europa_building_February_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Europa_building_February_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Europa_building_February_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Europa_building_February_2016_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Europa_building_February_2016_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Europa_building" title="Europa building">Europa building</a> (<b><a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a></b>)</div></div></div>
<p>The European Union operates through a hybrid system of <a href="/wiki/Supranational_union" title="Supranational union">supranational</a> and <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmentalism" title="Intergovernmentalism">intergovernmental</a> decision-making,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-140">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIA_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-141">[126]</a></sup> and according to the principles of <a href="/wiki/Principle_of_conferral" title="Principle of conferral">conferral</a> (which says that it should act only within the limits of the competences conferred on it by the <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">treaties</a>) and of <a href="/wiki/Subsidiarity_(European_Union)" title="Subsidiarity (European Union)">subsidiarity</a> (which says that it should act only where an objective cannot be sufficiently achieved by the member states acting alone). <a href="/wiki/European_Union_law" title="European Union law">Laws made by the EU institutions</a> are passed in a variety of forms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[127]</a></sup> Generally speaking, they can be classified into two groups: those which come into force without the necessity for national implementation measures (regulations) and those which specifically require national implementation measures (directives).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[128]</a></sup>
</p><p>EU policy is in general promulgated by <a href="/wiki/Directive_(European_Union)" title="Directive (European Union)">EU directives</a>, which are then implemented in the <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">domestic legislation</a> of its <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member states</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Regulation_(European_Union)" title="Regulation (European Union)">EU regulations</a>, which are immediately enforceable in all member states. <a href="/wiki/Lobbying#European_Union" title="Lobbying">Lobbying</a> at EU level by special interest groups is regulated to try to balance the aspirations of private initiatives with public interest decision-making process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[129]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_framework_and_legislation">Legal framework and legislation</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/European_Union_law" title="European Union law">European Union law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">Treaties of the European Union</a>, and <a href="/wiki/European_Union_legislative_procedure" title="European Union legislative procedure">European Union legislative procedure</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/European_Citizens%27_Initiative" title="European Citizens' Initiative">European Citizens' Initiative</a></div>
<p>Constitutionally, the EU bears some resemblance to both a <a href="/wiki/Confederation" title="Confederation">confederation</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federation</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[131]</a></sup> but has not formally defined itself as either. (It does not have a formal constitution: its status is defined by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_European_Union" title="Treaty of European Union">Treaty of European Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Functioning_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union">Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union</a>). It is more integrated than a traditional confederation of states because the general level of government widely employs <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qualified_majority_voting" title="Qualified majority voting">qualified majority voting</a> in some decision-making among the member states, rather than relying exclusively on unanimity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[133]</a></sup> It is less integrated than a federal state because it is not a state in its own right: sovereignty continues to flow 'from the bottom up', from the several peoples of the separate member states, rather than from a single undifferentiated whole. This is reflected in the fact that the member states remain the 'masters of the Treaties', retaining control over the allocation of competences to the union through constitutional change (thus retaining so-called <i>Kompetenz-kompetenz</i>); in that they retain control of the use of armed force; they retain control of taxation; and in that they retain a right of unilateral withdrawal under Article 50 of the Treaty on European Union. In addition, the principle of <a href="/wiki/Subsidiarity" title="Subsidiarity">subsidiarity</a> requires that only those matters that need to be determined collectively are so determined.
</p><p>Under the principle of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supremacy_(European_Union_law)" title="Supremacy (European Union law)">supremacy</a>, national courts are required to enforce the treaties that their member states have ratified, even if doing so requires them to ignore conflicting national law, and (within limits) even constitutional provisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Supremacy_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-Supremacy-149">[p]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct_effect" title="Direct effect">direct effect</a> and supremacy doctrines were not explicitly set out in the European Treaties but were developed by the Court of Justice itself over the 1960s, apparently under the influence of its then most influential judge, Frenchman <a href="/wiki/Robert_Lecourt" title="Robert Lecourt">Robert Lecourt</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[134]</a></sup> The question whether the secondary law enacted by the EU has a comparable  status in relation to national legistaltion, has been a matter of debate among legal scholars.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_law">Primary law</span></h4>
<p>The European Union is based on a series of <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">treaties</a>. These first established the European Community and the EU, and then made amendments to those founding treaties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[135]</a></sup> These are power-giving treaties which set broad policy goals and establish institutions with the necessary legal powers to implement those goals. These legal powers include the ability to enact legislation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-art249_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-art249-152">[q]</a></sup> which can directly affect all member states and their inhabitants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Direct_Effect_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Direct_Effect-153">[r]</a></sup> The EU has <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legal_personality" title="Legal personality">legal personality</a>, with the right to sign agreements and international treaties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[136]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_law">Secondary law</span></h4>
<p>The main legal acts of the European Union come in three forms: <a href="/wiki/Regulation_(European_Union)" title="Regulation (European Union)">regulations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Directive_(European_Union)" title="Directive (European Union)">directives</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Decision_(European_Union)" title="Decision (European Union)">decisions</a>. Regulations become law in all member states the moment they come into force, without the requirement for any implementing measures,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[s]</a></sup> and automatically override conflicting domestic provisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-art249_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-art249-152">[q]</a></sup> Directives require member states to achieve a certain result while leaving them discretion as to how to achieve the result. The details of how they are to be implemented are left to member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[t]</a></sup> When the time limit for implementing directives passes, they may, under certain conditions, have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct_effect" title="Direct effect">direct effect</a> in national law against member states. Decisions offer an alternative to the two above modes of legislation. They are legal acts which only apply to specified individuals, companies or a particular member state. They are most often used in <a href="/wiki/Competition_law" title="Competition law">competition law</a>, or on rulings on State Aid, but are also frequently used for procedural or administrative matters within the institutions. Regulations, directives, and decisions are of equal legal value and apply without any formal hierarchy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[137]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Safeguards">Safeguards</span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Ombudsman" title="European Ombudsman">European Ombudsman</a> was established by the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ombudsman" title="Ombudsman">ombudsman</a> is elected by the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> for the length of the parliament's term, and the position is renewable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[138]</a></sup> Any EU citizen or entity may appeal to the ombudsman to investigate an EU institution on the grounds of maladministration (administrative irregularities, unfairness, discrimination, abuse of power, failure to reply, refusal of information or unnecessary delay).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[139]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Emily_O%27Reilly" title="Emily O'Reilly">Emily O'Reilly</a> has been the ombudsman since 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[140]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Budget">Budget</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">Budget of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">
<div class="mw-no-invert" style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black;transform:scaleX(-1)rotate(-90deg)">
<div style="border:solid transparent;background-color: initial;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:lightblue"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;background-color: initial;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 932.64236482217px; border-left-color:green"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:green"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:green"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;background-color: initial;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 179.22262277715px; border-left-color:red"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:red"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:red"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;background-color: initial;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:47.070393216533px 88.229122643495px 0 0; border-top-color:brown"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:brown"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;background-color: initial;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:10.661115427526px 99.4300790397px 0 0; border-top-color:yellow"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:yellow"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;background-color: initial;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:0; border-width:0 114.87477060344px 100px 0; border-right-color:blue"></div>
<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;right:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 100px 0;border-color:blue"></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div style="text-align:center;"><b>EU funding programmes 2014-2020<br/>(€1,087 billion)</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[141]</a></sup></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:blue; color:white;"> </span> Sustainable Growth/Natural Resources (38.6%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:yellow; color:black;"> </span> Competitiveness for Growth and Jobs (13.1%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:brown; color:white;"> </span> Global Europe (6.1%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:red; color:black;"> </span> Economic, Territorial and Social Cohesion (34.1%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:green; color:white;"> </span> Administration (6.4%)</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:lightblue; color:black;"> </span> Security and Citizenship (1.7%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<p>The European Union had an agreed budget of €120.7 billion for the year 2007 and €864.3 billion for the period 2007–2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[142]</a></sup> representing 1.10 per cent and 1.05 per cent of the EU-27's <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_income" title="Gross national income">GNI</a> forecast for the respective periods. In 1960, the budget of the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Community</a> was 0.03 per cent of GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 2010 budget of €141.5 billion, the largest single expenditure item was "<i><a href="/wiki/European_Structural_and_Investment_Funds" title="European Structural and Investment Funds">cohesion &amp; competitiveness</a></i>" with around 45 per cent of the total budget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUBudget2010_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-EUBudget2010-164">[144]</a></sup> Next was "<i><a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">agriculture</a></i>" with approximately 31 per cent of the total.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUBudget2010_164-1"><a href="#cite_note-EUBudget2010-164">[144]</a></sup> "<i>Rural development, environment and <a href="/wiki/Common_Fisheries_Policy" title="Common Fisheries Policy">fisheries</a></i>" takes up around 11 per cent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUBudget2010_164-2"><a href="#cite_note-EUBudget2010-164">[144]</a></sup> "<i>Administration</i>" accounts for around 6 per cent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUBudget2010_164-3"><a href="#cite_note-EUBudget2010-164">[144]</a></sup> The "<i>EU as a global partner</i>" and "<i>citizenship, freedom, security and justice</i>" had approximately 6 per cent and 1 per cent respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUBudget2010_164-4"><a href="#cite_note-EUBudget2010-164">[144]</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2020, two members of the union, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, blocked approval to the EU's budget at a meeting in the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Permanent_Representatives" title="Committee of Permanent Representatives">Committee of Permanent Representatives</a> (Coreper), citing a <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_Law_Conditionality_Regulation" title="Rule of Law Conditionality Regulation">proposal that linked funding with adherence to the rule of law</a>. The budget included a <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19</a> recovery fund of €750<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion. The budget may still be approved if Hungary and Poland withdraw their vetoes after further negotiations in the council and the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[146]</a></sup>
</p><p>Bodies combatting fraud have also been established, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Anti-fraud_Office" title="European Anti-fraud Office">European Anti-fraud Office</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Public_Prosecutor%27s_Office" title="European Public Prosecutor's Office">European Public Prosecutor's Office</a>. The latter is a decentralized independent body of the European Union (EU), established under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a> between 22 of the 27 states of the EU following the method of <a href="/wiki/Enhanced_cooperation" title="Enhanced cooperation">enhanced cooperation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[147]</a></sup> The European Public Prosecutor's Office investigate and prosecute fraud against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU_budget" title="EU budget">budget of the European Union</a> and other crimes against the EU's financial interests including fraud concerning EU funds of over €10,000 and cross-border <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Value_added_tax" title="Value added tax">VAT</a> fraud cases involving damages above €10 million.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Bodies_of_the_European_Union_and_the_Euratom" title="Bodies of the European Union and the Euratom">Bodies of the European Union and the Euratom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Institutions_of_the_European_Union" title="Institutions of the European Union">Institutions of the European Union</a></div>
<p>Member states retain in principle all powers not conferred by them on the European Union, though the exact delimitation has on many occasions become a subject of scholarly or legal disputes. Inspired by the famous <a href="/wiki/Commerce_Clause" title="Commerce Clause">Commerce Clause</a> and the huge impact that its interpretation and mode of application by the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a> had on shaping the American federal government, the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Justice_of_the_European_Union" title="Court of Justice of the European Union">Court of Justice of the European Union</a> has sometimes managed to expand through its case law the powers of the EU, including those related to areas other than only the ones explicitly conferred on it in the founding treaties.
</p><p>In certain fields the EU has been awarded exclusive competence and <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_mandate" title="Exclusive mandate">mandate</a>. These are areas in which member states have entirely renounced their own capacity to enact legislation. In other areas the EU and its member states share the competence to legislate. While both can legislate, member states can only legislate to the extent to which the EU has not. In other policy areas the EU can only co-ordinate, support and supplement member state action but cannot enact legislation with the aim of harmonising national laws.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[148]</a></sup> That a particular policy area falls into a certain category of competence is not necessarily indicative of what <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislature_of_the_European_Union" title="Legislature of the European Union">legislative procedure</a> is used for enacting legislation within that policy area. Different legislative procedures are used within the same category of competence, and even with the same policy area. The distribution of competences in various policy areas between member states and the union is divided in the following three categories:
</p>
<table style="width:100%;background:none;">

</td></tr></tbody></table>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The European Union has seven principal decision-making bodies, its <a href="/wiki/Institutions_of_the_European_Union" title="Institutions of the European Union">institutions</a>: the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Justice_of_the_European_Union" title="Court of Justice of the European Union">Court of Justice of the European Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Auditors" title="European Court of Auditors">European Court of Auditors</a>. Competence in scrutinising and amending legislation is shared between the Council of the European Union and the European Parliament, while executive tasks are performed by the European Commission and in a limited capacity by the European Council (not to be confused with the aforementioned Council of the European Union). The <a href="/wiki/Monetary_policy" title="Monetary policy">monetary policy</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> is determined by the European Central Bank. The interpretation and the application of EU law and the treaties are ensured by the Court of Justice of the European Union. The EU budget is scrutinised by the European Court of Auditors. There are also a number of ancillary bodies which advise the EU or operate in a specific area.
</p>
<div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><b>Political <a href="/wiki/Institutions_of_the_European_Union" title="Institutions of the European Union">institutions of the European Union</a></b></div>

<td>Based in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>.
