</td>
<td>Based in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>. Meets in <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">Luxembourg</a>, <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg/23px-Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg/35px-Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg/46px-Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> for the months of April, June and October.
</td>
<td>Meets in <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a>, <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>, <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_Belgium_%28civil%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>. Secretariat based in <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">Luxembourg</a>, <span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg/23px-Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg/35px-Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg/46px-Flag_of_Luxembourg.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>.
</td></tr>
<tr style="background: #F2F2F2;">
<td style="padding-bottom: 1em; padding-left: 1.5em; vertical-align: top;">Described as the union's "supreme political leadership",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-How_work_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-How_work-170">[150]</a></sup> it acts as a "<a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">collective head of state</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Ratification" title="Ratification">ratifies</a> important documents (for example, international agreements and treaties),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oxford_University_Press_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oxford_University_Press-171">[151]</a></sup> as well as sets the broad <i>general political directions</i> and <i>priorities</i> of the Union identified by its member states' <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">heads of state</a>/<a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">government</a> (elected chief executives). The conclusions of its summits (held at least quarterly) are adopted by consensus, while translating them into practical solutions is the task of the EU Commission's agenda.
</td>
<td style="vertical-align: top; padding-left: 15px; padding-bottom: 10px;">The body is shaped as the  <i>College of Commissioners</i>, an <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">executive cabinet</a> composed of politicians holding various portfolios, under the leadership of its president, all of them expected to align only with their respective <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Parliament_political_group" title="European Parliament political group">European Parliament political groups</a> while  remaining impartial in respect to their own or any other member state governments. Although candidates for the posts of the President or the commissioners have remained <a href="/wiki/Indirect_election" title="Indirect election">selected indirectly</a> by the member states, the President and the designated cabinet are responsible to the Parliament and must obtain its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vote_of_confidence" title="Vote of confidence">vote of confidence</a>. Designated as the "Guardian of the Treaties", it is the primary source of draft EU legislation, with its agenda shaped broadely by the consensus objectives defined by the European Council and aiming to translate them into tangible and working <a href="/wiki/European_Union_law" title="European Union law">EU legislation</a>.
</td>
<td style="padding-bottom: 1em; padding-left: 1.5em; vertical-align: top;">Brings together ministers of member states governments' departments. It enables the national governments to express directly their stance, and grants the approval necessary for any draft legislation to become law.
</td>
<td style="padding-bottom: 1em; padding-left: 1.5em; vertical-align: top;">Consists of 705 directly elected representatives. It shares with the Council of the EU equal legislative powers to amend, approve or reject Commission proposals for most areas of EU legislation. Its powers are limited in areas where member states' view sovereignty to be of primary concern (i.e. defence). It elects the commission's president, must approve the College of Commissioners, and may vote to remove them collectively from office.
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive">Executive</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Council">European Council</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Michel_(49467991288).jpg"><img alt="Portrait of Charles Michel" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="2667" decoding="async" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Charles_Michel_%2849467991288%29.jpg/130px-Charles_Michel_%2849467991288%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Charles_Michel_%2849467991288%29.jpg/195px-Charles_Michel_%2849467991288%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Charles_Michel_%2849467991288%29.jpg/260px-Charles_Michel_%2849467991288%29.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Michel_(49467991288).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Charles_Michel" title="Charles Michel">Charles Michel</a><br/><small><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">President of the European Council</a></small></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a></div>
<p>The European Council sets the broad political direction to the EU. It convenes at least four times a year and comprises the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">president of the European Council</a> (presently <a href="/wiki/Charles_Michel" title="Charles Michel">Charles Michel</a>), the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">president of the European Commission</a> and one representative per <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member state</a> (either its <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> or <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>). The <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy" title="High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy">high representative of the union for foreign affairs and security policy</a> (presently <a href="/wiki/Josep_Borrell" title="Josep Borrell">Josep Borrell</a>) also takes part in its meetings. Described by some as the union's "supreme political leadership",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-How_work_170-1"><a href="#cite_note-How_work-170">[150]</a></sup> it is actively involved in the negotiation of <a href="/wiki/Treaties_of_the_European_Union" title="Treaties of the European Union">treaty changes</a> and defines the EU's policy agenda and strategies. Its leadership role involves solving disputes between member states and the institutions, and to resolving any political crises or disagreements over controversial issues and policies. It acts as a "<a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">collective head of state</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Ratification" title="Ratification">ratifies</a> important documents (for example, international agreements and treaties).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oxford_University_Press_171-1"><a href="#cite_note-Oxford_University_Press-171">[151]</a></sup>
</p><p>Tasks for the president of the European Council are ensuring the external representation of the EU,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Council_Press_Release_172-0"><a href="#cite_note-Council_Press_Release-172">[152]</a></sup> driving consensus and resolving divergences among member states, both during meetings of the European Council and over the periods between them.
</p><p>The European Council should not be mistaken for the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, an international organisation independent of the EU and based in Strasbourg.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Commission">European Commission</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ursula_von_der_Leyen_(49468709252).jpg"><img alt="Portrait of Ursula von der Leyen" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1378" data-file-width="919" decoding="async" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Ursula_von_der_Leyen_%2849468709252%29.jpg/130px-Ursula_von_der_Leyen_%2849468709252%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Ursula_von_der_Leyen_%2849468709252%29.jpg/195px-Ursula_von_der_Leyen_%2849468709252%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Ursula_von_der_Leyen_%2849468709252%29.jpg/260px-Ursula_von_der_Leyen_%2849468709252%29.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ursula_von_der_Leyen_(49468709252).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ursula_von_der_Leyen" title="Ursula von der Leyen">Ursula von der Leyen</a><br/><small><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">President of the European Commission</a></small></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a></div>
<p>The European Commission acts both as the EU's <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive arm</a>, responsible for the day-to-day running of the EU, and also the <a href="/wiki/Right_of_initiative_(legislative)" title="Right of initiative (legislative)">legislative initiator</a>, with the sole power to propose laws for debate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Library_of_European_Parliament_174-0"><a href="#cite_note-Library_of_European_Parliament-174">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[155]</a></sup> The commission is 'guardian of the Treaties' and is responsible for their efficient operation and policing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[156]</a></sup> It has 27 <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner" title="European Commissioner">European commissioners</a> for different areas of policy, one from each member state, though commissioners are bound to represent the interests of the EU as a whole rather than their home state.
</p><p>The leader of the 27 is the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">president of the European Commission</a> (presently <a href="/wiki/Ursula_von_der_Leyen" title="Ursula von der Leyen">Ursula von der Leyen</a> for 2019–2024), <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission#Appointment" title="President of the European Commission">proposed by the European Council</a>, following and taking into account the result of the European elections, and is then elected by the European Parliament.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[157]</a></sup>  The President retains, as the leader responsible for the entire cabinet, the final say in accepting or rejecting a candidate submitted for a given portfolio by a member state, and oversees the commission's permanent civil service. After the President, the most prominent commissioner is the high representative of the union for foreign affairs and security policy, who is <i>ex-officio</i> a <a href="/wiki/Vice-President_of_the_European_Commission" title="Vice-President of the European Commission">vice-president of the European Commission</a> and is also chosen by the European Council.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[158]</a></sup> The other 26 commissioners are subsequently appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a> in agreement with the nominated president. The 27 commissioners as a single body are subject to approval (or otherwise) by vote of the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a>. All commissioners are first nominated by the government of the respective member state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[159]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislature">Legislature</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Council_of_the_European_Union">Council of the European Union</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg"><img alt="Flag of the Czech Republic" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" decoding="async" height="87" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/130px-Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/195px-Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/260px-Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png 2x" width="130"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a><br/><small><a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_the_Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Presidency of the Council of the European Union">Presidency of the Council of the European Union</a></small></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a></div>
<p>The Council of the European Union (also called the Council<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[160]</a></sup> and the "Council of Ministers", its former title)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[161]</a></sup> forms one half of the EU's legislature. It consists of a representative from each member state's government and meets in <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union#Configurations" title="Council of the European Union">different compositions depending on the policy area being addressed</a>. Notwithstanding its different configurations, it is considered to be one single body. In addition to the legislative functions, members of the council also have <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a> responsibilities, such as the development of a <a href="/wiki/Common_Foreign_and_Security_Policy" title="Common Foreign and Security Policy">Common Foreign and Security Policy</a> and the coordination of broad economic policies within the Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Institutions_Council_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Institutions_Council-182">[162]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_the_Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Presidency of the Council of the European Union">Presidency of the council</a> rotates between member states, with each holding it for six months. Beginning on 1 July 2022, the position is held by the Czech Republic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[163]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Parliament">European Parliament</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roberta_Metsola_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="Portrait of Roberta Metsola" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1696" data-file-width="1455" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Roberta_Metsola_%28cropped%29.jpg/130px-Roberta_Metsola_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Roberta_Metsola_%28cropped%29.jpg/195px-Roberta_Metsola_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Roberta_Metsola_%28cropped%29.jpg/260px-Roberta_Metsola_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roberta_Metsola_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Roberta_Metsola" title="Roberta Metsola">Roberta Metsola</a><br/><small><a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Parliament" title="President of the European Parliament">President of the European Parliament</a></small></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SOTEU_2022_(52358409262).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1986" data-file-width="3000" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/SOTEU_2022_%2852358409262%29.jpg/220px-SOTEU_2022_%2852358409262%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/SOTEU_2022_%2852358409262%29.jpg/330px-SOTEU_2022_%2852358409262%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/SOTEU_2022_%2852358409262%29.jpg/440px-SOTEU_2022_%2852358409262%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SOTEU_2022_(52358409262).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> represents the second-largest democratic electorate in the world (after the Parliament of India)</div></div></div>
<p>The European Parliament is one of three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislature_of_the_European_Union" title="Legislature of the European Union">legislative institutions</a> of the EU, which together with the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_European_Union" title="Council of the European Union">Council of the European Union</a> is tasked with amending and approving the European Commission's proposals. 705 <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">members of the European Parliament</a> (MEPs) are directly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_European_Union" title="Elections in the European Union">elected</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_European_Union" title="Citizenship of the European Union">EU citizens</a> every five years on the basis of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a>. MEPs are elected on a national basis and they sit according to <a href="/wiki/Political_groups_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Political groups of the European Parliament">political groups</a> rather than their nationality. Each country has a set number of seats and is divided into <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_constituency" title="European Parliament constituency">sub-national constituencies</a> where this does not affect the proportional nature of the voting system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[164]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ordinary_legislative_procedure" title="Ordinary legislative procedure">ordinary legislative procedure</a>, the European Commission proposes legislation, which requires the joint approval of the European Parliament and the Council of the European Union to pass. This process applies to nearly all areas, including the <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">EU budget</a>. The parliament is the final body to approve or reject the proposed membership of the commission, and can attempt motions of censure on the commission by appeal to the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Justice" title="European Court of Justice">Court of Justice</a>. The <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Parliament" title="President of the European Parliament">president of the European Parliament</a> carries out the role of speaker in Parliament and represents it externally. The president and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Vice President of the European Parliament">vice-presidents</a> are elected by MEPs every two and a half years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Institutions_Parliament_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Institutions_Parliament-185">[165]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judiciary">Judiciary</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Court_of_Justice_of_the_European_Union">Court of Justice of the European Union</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Justice_of_the_European_Union" title="Court of Justice of the European Union">Court of Justice of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palais_de_la_Cour_de_Justice_CJEU_July_2021_Sign_and_Towers_B_and_C.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1308" data-file-width="1394" decoding="async" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Palais_de_la_Cour_de_Justice_CJEU_July_2021_Sign_and_Towers_B_and_C.jpg/220px-Palais_de_la_Cour_de_Justice_CJEU_July_2021_Sign_and_Towers_B_and_C.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Palais_de_la_Cour_de_Justice_CJEU_July_2021_Sign_and_Towers_B_and_C.jpg/330px-Palais_de_la_Cour_de_Justice_CJEU_July_2021_Sign_and_Towers_B_and_C.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Palais_de_la_Cour_de_Justice_CJEU_July_2021_Sign_and_Towers_B_and_C.jpg/440px-Palais_de_la_Cour_de_Justice_CJEU_July_2021_Sign_and_Towers_B_and_C.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palais_de_la_Cour_de_Justice_CJEU_July_2021_Sign_and_Towers_B_and_C.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The CJEU's seat, the <a href="/wiki/Palais_de_la_Cour_de_Justice" title="Palais de la Cour de Justice">Palais de la Cour de Justice</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">Luxembourg City</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judicial branch</a> of the European Union is formally called the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Justice_of_the_European_Union" title="Court of Justice of the European Union">Court of Justice of the European Union</a> and consists of two courts: the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Justice" title="European Court of Justice">Court of Justice</a> and the <a href="/wiki/General_Court_(European_Union)" title="General Court (European Union)">General Court</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[166]</a></sup> The Court of Justice primarily deals with cases taken by member states, the institutions, and <a href="/wiki/Preliminary_ruling" title="Preliminary ruling">cases referred to it</a> by the courts of member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[167]</a></sup> Because of the doctrines of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct_effect" title="Direct effect">direct effect</a> and supremacy, many judgments of the Court of Justice are automatically applicable within the internal legal orders of the member states.
</p><p>The General Court mainly deals with cases taken by individuals and companies directly before the EU's courts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[168]</a></sup> and the European Union Civil Service Tribunal adjudicates in disputes between the European Union and <a href="/wiki/European_Civil_Service" title="European Civil Service">its civil service</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[169]</a></sup> Decisions from the General Court can be appealed to the Court of Justice but only on a point of law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[170]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_institutions">Other institutions</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Court_of_Auditors">European Court of Auditors</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Auditors" title="European Court of Auditors">European Court of Auditors</a></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Court_of_Auditors" title="Court of Auditors">Court of Auditors</a> is legally obliged to provide the parliament and the council (specifically, the <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_Financial_Affairs_Council" title="Economic and Financial Affairs Council">Economic and Financial Affairs Council</a>) with "a statement of assurance as to the reliability of the accounts and the legality and regularity of the underlying transactions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[171]</a></sup> The Court also gives opinions and proposals on financial legislation and anti-fraud actions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Institutions_Auditors_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Institutions_Auditors-192">[172]</a></sup> The parliament uses this to decide whether to approve the commission's handling of the budget.
</p><p>The European Court of Auditors has signed off the European Union accounts every year since 2007 and, while making it clear that the European Commission has more work to do, has highlighted that most of the errors take place at national level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-European_Court_of_Auditors_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-European_Court_of_Auditors-193">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-European_Commission_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-European_Commission-194">[174]</a></sup> In their report on 2009 the auditors found that five areas of Union expenditure, <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">agriculture</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Structural_Funds_and_Cohesion_Fund" title="Structural Funds and Cohesion Fund">cohesion fund</a>, were materially affected by error.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[175]</a></sup> The European Commission estimated in 2009 that the financial effect of irregularities was €1,863 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[176]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Central_Bank">European Central Bank</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_System_of_Central_Banks" title="European System of Central Banks">European System of Central Banks</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a> is at the centre of the <a href="/wiki/European_System_of_Central_Banks" title="European System of Central Banks">European System of Central Banks</a>, which comprehends all EU national central banks and is controlled by its General Council, consisting of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Central_Bank" title="President of the European Central Bank">President of the ECB</a>, who is appointed by the European Council, the vice-president of the ECB, and the governors of the national central banks of all 27 EU member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ECB_org_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-ECB_org-197">[177]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_European_Union" title="Economy of the European Union">Economy of the European Union</a></div>
<p>As a political entity, the European Union is represented in the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO). EU member states own the estimated second largest after the United States (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$105</span><span class="nowrap"> </span>trillion) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Net_wealth" title="Net wealth">net wealth</a> in the world, equal to around 20 per cent (~€60<span class="nowrap"> </span>trillion) of the <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$36</span><span class="nowrap"> </span>trillion (~€300<span class="nowrap"> </span>trillion)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[178]</a></sup> global wealth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[179]</a></sup>
</p><p>Of the top <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">500 largest corporations in the world measured by revenue</a> in 2010, 161 had their headquarters in the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[180]</a></sup> In 2016, unemployment in the EU stood at 8.9 per cent<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNEMP_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNEMP-201">[181]</a></sup> while inflation was at 2.2 per cent, and the account balance at −0.9 per cent of GDP. The average annual net earnings in the European Union was around €24,000 (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$30,000</span>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[182]</a></sup> in 2015.
</p><p>There is a significant variation in nominal GDP per capita within individual EU states. The difference between the richest and poorest regions (281 NUTS-2 regions of the <a href="/wiki/Nomenclature_of_Territorial_Units_for_Statistics" title="Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics">Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics</a>) ranged, in 2017, from 31 per cent (Severozapaden, Bulgaria) of the EU28 average (€30,000) to 253 per cent (Luxembourg), or from €4,600 to €92,600.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[183]</a></sup>
</p><p>Two of the original core objectives of the European Economic Community were the development of a common market, subsequently becoming a <a href="/wiki/Single_market" title="Single market">single market</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">customs union</a> between its member states.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Customs_union_and_external_trade_policy">Customs union and external trade policy</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">European Union Customs Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Common_Commercial_Policy_(EU)" title="Common Commercial Policy (EU)">Common Commercial Policy (EU)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Batumi_International_Conference,_on_19_July_2021_05_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1699" data-file-width="2548" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Batumi_International_Conference%2C_on_19_July_2021_05_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Batumi_International_Conference%2C_on_19_July_2021_05_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Batumi_International_Conference%2C_on_19_July_2021_05_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Batumi_International_Conference%2C_on_19_July_2021_05_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Batumi_International_Conference%2C_on_19_July_2021_05_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Batumi_International_Conference%2C_on_19_July_2021_05_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Batumi_International_Conference,_on_19_July_2021_05_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President of Georgia <a href="/wiki/Salome_Zourabichvili" title="Salome Zourabichvili">Salome Zourabichvili</a>, President of <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a> <a href="/wiki/Maia_Sandu" title="Maia Sandu">Maia Sandu</a>, President of Ukraine <a href="/wiki/Volodymyr_Zelenskyy" title="Volodymyr Zelenskyy">Volodymyr Zelenskyy</a> and <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Council" title="President of the European Council">President of the European Council</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Michel" title="Charles Michel">Charles Michel</a> during the 2021 <a href="/wiki/Batumi" title="Batumi">Batumi</a> International Conference. In 2014, the EU signed <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Association_Agreement" title="European Union Association Agreement">Association Agreements</a> with all the three states.</div></div></div>
<p>The customs union involves the application of a <a href="/wiki/Common_external_tariff" title="Common external tariff">common external tariff</a> on all goods entering the market. Once goods have been admitted into the market they cannot be subjected to customs duties, discriminatory taxes or <a href="/wiki/Import_quota" title="Import quota">import quotas</a>, as they travel internally. The non-EU member states of <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a> and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> participate in the single market but not in the customs union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EEA_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-EEA-135">[122]</a></sup> Half the trade in the EU is covered by legislation harmonised by the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Single_Market_G_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Single_Market_G-204">[184]</a></sup>
</p><p>The European Union is the largest exporter in the world<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[185]</a></sup> and in 2008 was the largest importer of goods and services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[187]</a></sup> Internal trade between the member states is aided by the removal of barriers to trade such as <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">tariffs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Border_control" title="Border control">border controls</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a>, trade is helped by not having any currency differences to deal with amongst most members.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Se-jeong_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-Se-jeong-208">[188]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Association_Agreement" title="European Union Association Agreement">European Union Association Agreement</a> does something similar for a much larger range of countries, partly as a so-called soft approach ('a carrot instead of a stick') to influence the politics in those countries.
The European Union represents all its members at the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO), and acts on behalf of member states in any disputes. When the EU negotiates trade related agreement outside the WTO framework, the subsequent agreement must be approved by each individual EU member state government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Se-jeong_208-1"><a href="#cite_note-Se-jeong-208">[188]</a></sup>
</p><p>The European Union has concluded <a href="/wiki/European_Union_free_trade_agreements" title="European Union free trade agreements">free trade agreements</a> (FTAs)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[189]</a></sup> and other agreements with a trade component with many countries worldwide and is negotiating with many others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[190]</a></sup>
</p><p>The European Union's services trade surplus rose from $16 billion in 2000 to more than $250 billion in 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[191]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, in part due to the COVID-19 pandemic, China became the EU's largest trading partner, displacing the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[192]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Single_market">Single market</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Single_Market" title="European Single Market">European Single Market</a> and <a href="/wiki/Digital_Single_Market" title="Digital Single Market">Digital Single Market</a></div>
<p>The single market involves <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_market" title="Internal market">the free circulation of goods, capital, people, and services within the EU</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Single_Market_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Single_Market-213">[193]</a></sup>
</p><p>The free movement of services and of establishment allows self-employed persons to move between member states to provide services on a temporary or permanent basis. While services account for 60 per cent to 70 per cent of GDP, legislation in the area is not as developed as in other areas. This lacuna has been addressed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Services_in_the_Internal_Market_Directive_2006" title="Services in the Internal Market Directive 2006">Services in the Internal Market Directive 2006</a> which aims to liberalise the cross border provision of services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Single_Market_S_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Single_Market_S-214">[194]</a></sup> According to the treaty the provision of services is a residual freedom that only applies if no other freedom is being exercised.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition_and_consumer_protection">Competition and consumer protection</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/European_Union_competition_law" title="European Union competition law">European Union competition law</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_consumer_law" title="European consumer law">European consumer law</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_Competition" title="European Commissioner for Competition">European Commissioner for Competition</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Docks" title="Silicon Docks">Silicon Docks</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:264px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Plug-in_power_adapter_USB_for_Apple,_Model_A1300,_by_Flextronics-0813.jpg"><img alt="CE marking example" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2562" data-file-width="4555" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Plug-in_power_adapter_USB_for_Apple%2C_Model_A1300%2C_by_Flextronics-0813.jpg/262px-Plug-in_power_adapter_USB_for_Apple%2C_Model_A1300%2C_by_Flextronics-0813.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Plug-in_power_adapter_USB_for_Apple%2C_Model_A1300%2C_by_Flextronics-0813.jpg/393px-Plug-in_power_adapter_USB_for_Apple%2C_Model_A1300%2C_by_Flextronics-0813.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Plug-in_power_adapter_USB_for_Apple%2C_Model_A1300%2C_by_Flextronics-0813.jpg/524px-Plug-in_power_adapter_USB_for_Apple%2C_Model_A1300%2C_by_Flextronics-0813.jpg 2x" width="262"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Plug-in_power_adapter_USB_for_Apple,_Model_A1300,_by_Flextronics-0813.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/CE_marking" title="CE marking">CE conformity marking</a> on a mobile phone charger.</div></div></div>
<p>The EU operates a <a href="/wiki/European_Union_competition_law" title="European Union competition law">competition policy</a> intended to ensure undistorted competition within the single market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[u]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2001 the commission for the first time prevented a merger between two companies based in the United States (<a href="/wiki/General_Electric" title="General Electric">General Electric</a> and <a href="/wiki/Honeywell" title="Honeywell">Honeywell</a>) which had already been approved by their national authority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[195]</a></sup> Another high-profile case, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Union_Microsoft_competition_case" title="European Union Microsoft competition case">against Microsoft</a>, resulted in the commission fining <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> over €777 million following nine years of legal action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[196]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_policy_of_the_European_Union" title="Energy policy of the European Union">Energy policy of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;">
<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:300px; background: white;">
