</div>
</div>
<p>In 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Accession_2005" title="Treaty of Accession 2005">EU-27</a> had a gross inland energy consumption of 1,825 million tonnes of oil equivalent (toe).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EurostatEnergy_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-EurostatEnergy-219">[197]</a></sup> Around 46 per cent of the energy consumed was produced within the member states while 54 per cent was imported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EurostatEnergy_219-1"><a href="#cite_note-EurostatEnergy-219">[197]</a></sup> In these statistics, nuclear energy is treated as <a href="/wiki/Primary_energy" title="Primary energy">primary energy</a> produced in the EU, regardless of the source of the uranium, of which less than 3 per cent is produced in the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Euratom2007_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-Euratom2007-220">[198]</a></sup>
</p><p>The EU has had legislative power in the area of energy policy for most of its existence; this has its roots in the original <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a>. The introduction of a mandatory and comprehensive European energy policy was approved at the meeting of the European Council in October 2005, and the first draft policy was published in January 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Energy_Q&amp;A_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-Energy_Q&amp;A-221">[199]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="635" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg/300px-20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg/450px-20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg/600px-20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:20210125_Europe_Power_Sector_-_Renewables_vs_Fossil_Fuels_-_Climate_change.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In 2020, renewables overtook fossil fuels as the European Union's main source of electricity for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EmberEUpower_20210125_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-EmberEUpower_20210125-222">[200]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The EU has five key points in its energy policy: increase competition in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_market" title="Internal market">internal market</a>, encourage investment and boost interconnections between electricity grids; diversify energy resources with better systems to respond to a crisis; establish a new treaty framework for energy co-operation with Russia while improving relations with energy-rich states in Central Asia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oies_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-oies-223">[201]</a></sup> and North Africa; use existing energy supplies more efficiently while increasing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_commercialisation" title="Renewable energy commercialisation">renewable energy commercialisation</a>; and finally increase funding for new energy technologies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Energy_Q&amp;A_221-1"><a href="#cite_note-Energy_Q&amp;A-221">[199]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, EU countries as a whole imported 82 per cent of their oil, 57 per cent of their natural gas<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-low_carb_prop_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-low_carb_prop-224">[202]</a></sup> and 97.48 per cent of their uranium<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Euratom2007_220-1"><a href="#cite_note-Euratom2007-220">[198]</a></sup> demands. The three largest suppliers of natural gas to the European Union are Russia, Norway and <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, that amounted for about three quarters of the imports in 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[203]</a></sup> There is a strong <a href="/wiki/Russia_in_the_European_energy_sector" title="Russia in the European energy sector">dependence on Russian energy</a> that the EU has been attempting to reduce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Energy_Russia_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-Energy_Russia-226">[204]</a></sup> However, in May 2022, it was reported that the European Union is preparing another sanction against Russia over its invasion of Ukraine. It is expected to target Russian oil, Russian and Belarusian banks, as well as individuals and companies. According to an article by Reuters, two diplomats stated that the European Union may impose a ban on imports of Russian oil by the end of 2022.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[205]</a></sup> In May 2022, the EU Commission published the 'RePowerEU' initiative, a €300 billion plan outlining the path towards the end of EU dependence on Russian fossil fuels by 2030 and the acceleration on the clean energy transition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[206]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure_and_transport">Infrastructure and transport</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Trans-European_Networks" title="Trans-European Networks">Trans-European Networks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_European_Union" title="Transport in the European Union">Transport in the European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Common_Aviation_Area" title="European Common Aviation Area">European Common Aviation Area</a>, <a href="/wiki/Single_European_Sky" title="Single European Sky">Single European Sky</a>, and <a href="/wiki/European_Rail_Traffic_Management_System" title="European Rail Traffic Management System">European Rail Traffic Management System</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%C3%98resund_Bridge_from_the_air_in_September_2015.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/%C3%98resund_Bridge_from_the_air_in_September_2015.jpg/170px-%C3%98resund_Bridge_from_the_air_in_September_2015.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/%C3%98resund_Bridge_from_the_air_in_September_2015.jpg/255px-%C3%98resund_Bridge_from_the_air_in_September_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/%C3%98resund_Bridge_from_the_air_in_September_2015.jpg/340px-%C3%98resund_Bridge_from_the_air_in_September_2015.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%C3%98resund_Bridge_from_the_air_in_September_2015.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/%C3%98resund_Bridge" title="Øresund Bridge">Öresund Bridge</a> between Denmark and Sweden is part of the <a href="/wiki/Trans-European_Networks" title="Trans-European Networks">Trans-European Networks</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The European Union is working to improve cross-border infrastructure, for example through the <a href="/wiki/Trans-European_Networks" title="Trans-European Networks">Trans-European Networks</a> (TEN). Projects under TEN include the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Tunnel" title="Channel Tunnel">Channel Tunnel</a>, <a href="/wiki/LGV_Est" title="LGV Est">LGV Est</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9jus_Rail_Tunnel" title="Fréjus Rail Tunnel">Fréjus Rail Tunnel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/%C3%98resund_Bridge" title="Øresund Bridge">Öresund Bridge</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Brenner_Base_Tunnel" title="Brenner Base Tunnel">Brenner Base Tunnel</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Messina_Bridge" title="Strait of Messina Bridge">Strait of Messina Bridge</a>. In 2010 the estimated network covers: 75,200 kilometres (46,700 mi) of roads; 78,000 kilometres (48,000 mi) of railways; 330 airports; 270 maritime harbours; and 210 internal harbours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[207]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[208]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Europe" title="Rail transport in Europe">Rail transport in Europe</a> is being synchronised with the <a href="/wiki/European_Rail_Traffic_Management_System" title="European Rail Traffic Management System">European Rail Traffic Management System</a> (ERTMS), an initiative to greatly enhance safety, increase efficiency of trains and enhance cross-border interoperability of rail transport in Europe by replacing signalling equipment with digitised mostly wireless versions and by creating a single Europe-wide standard for train control and command systems.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The developing European transport policies will increase the pressure on the environment in many regions by the increased transport network. In the pre-2004 EU members, the major problem in transport deals with congestion and pollution. After the recent enlargement, the new states that joined since 2004 added the problem of solving accessibility to the transport agenda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[209]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Highways_in_Poland" title="Highways in Poland">Polish road network</a> was upgraded such as the <a href="/wiki/A4_autostrada_(Poland)" title="A4 autostrada (Poland)">A4 autostrada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[210]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Telecommunications.2C_armaments_and_space"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecommunications,_armaments_and_space">Telecommunications, armaments and space</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/European_Union_roaming_regulations" title="European Union roaming regulations">European Union roaming regulations</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Space_Programme" title="European Union Space Programme">European Union Space Programme</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galileo_Control_Centre_at_the_DLR_Oberpfaffenhofen_site.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="997" data-file-width="1772" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Galileo_Control_Centre_at_the_DLR_Oberpfaffenhofen_site.jpg/220px-Galileo_Control_Centre_at_the_DLR_Oberpfaffenhofen_site.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Galileo_Control_Centre_at_the_DLR_Oberpfaffenhofen_site.jpg/330px-Galileo_Control_Centre_at_the_DLR_Oberpfaffenhofen_site.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Galileo_Control_Centre_at_the_DLR_Oberpfaffenhofen_site.jpg/440px-Galileo_Control_Centre_at_the_DLR_Oberpfaffenhofen_site.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Galileo_Control_Centre_at_the_DLR_Oberpfaffenhofen_site.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Galileo Control Centre at the DLR Oberpfaffenhofen site</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galileo_IOT_L-band_antenna_at_Redu_ESA219283.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2368" data-file-width="3552" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Galileo_IOT_L-band_antenna_at_Redu_ESA219283.jpg/220px-Galileo_IOT_L-band_antenna_at_Redu_ESA219283.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Galileo_IOT_L-band_antenna_at_Redu_ESA219283.jpg/330px-Galileo_IOT_L-band_antenna_at_Redu_ESA219283.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Galileo_IOT_L-band_antenna_at_Redu_ESA219283.jpg/440px-Galileo_IOT_L-band_antenna_at_Redu_ESA219283.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Galileo_IOT_L-band_antenna_at_Redu_ESA219283.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Galileo In-Orbit Test (IOT) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L-band" title="L-band">L-band</a> antenna at <a href="/wiki/ESTRACK" title="ESTRACK">ESTRACK</a> <a href="/wiki/Redu_Station" title="Redu Station">Redu Station</a></div></div></div>
<p>Mobile communication <a href="/wiki/European_Union_roaming_regulations" title="European Union roaming regulations">roaming charges</a> are abolished throughout the EU, Iceland, Liechtenstein and Norway.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Galileo_(satellite_navigation)" title="Galileo (satellite navigation)">Galileo positioning system</a> is an EU infrastructure project. Galileo is a proposed <a href="/wiki/Satellite_navigation" title="Satellite navigation">Satellite navigation</a> system, to be built by the EU and launched by the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a> (ESA). The Galileo project was launched partly to reduce the EU's dependency on the US-operated <a href="/wiki/Global_Positioning_System" title="Global Positioning System">Global Positioning System</a>, but also to give more complete global coverage and allow for greater accuracy, given the aged nature of the GPS system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barrot_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barrot-233">[211]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture_and_fisheries">Agriculture and fisheries</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">Common Agricultural Policy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Common_Fisheries_Policy" title="Common Fisheries Policy">Common Fisheries Policy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg/220px-RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg/330px-RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg/440px-RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RO_BZ_Pietroasele_vineyard.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Vineyards in Romania; EU farms are supported by the <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">Common Agricultural Policy</a>, the largest <a href="/wiki/Budget_of_the_European_Union" title="Budget of the European Union">budgetary</a> expenditure.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">Common Agricultural Policy</a> (CAP) is one of the long lasting policies of the European Community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stead_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-stead-234">[212]</a></sup> The policy has the objectives of increasing agricultural production, providing certainty in food supplies, ensuring a high quality of life for farmers, stabilising markets, and ensuring reasonable prices for consumers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[w]</a></sup> It was, until recently, operated by a system of subsidies and market intervention. Until the 1990s, the policy accounted for over 60 per cent of the European Community's annual budget, and in 2013 accounted for around 34 per cent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EU_CAP_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-EU_CAP-236">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>The policy's <a href="/wiki/Incomes_policy" title="Incomes policy">price controls</a> and market interventions led to considerable <a href="/wiki/Overproduction" title="Overproduction">overproduction</a>. These were <a href="/wiki/Buffer_stock_scheme" title="Buffer stock scheme">intervention stores</a> of products bought up by the community to maintain minimum price levels. To dispose of surplus stores, they were often sold on the world market at prices considerably below Community guaranteed prices, or farmers were offered subsidies (amounting to the difference between the community and world prices) to export their products outside the community. This system has been criticised for under-cutting farmers outside Europe, especially those in the <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">developing world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_CAP_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_CAP-237">[214]</a></sup> Supporters of CAP argue that the economic support which it gives to farmers provides them with a reasonable <a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">standard of living</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_CAP_237-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_CAP-237">[214]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the beginning of the 1990s, the CAP has been subject to a series of reforms. Initially, these reforms included the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Set-aside" title="Set-aside">set-aside</a> in 1988, where a proportion of farm land was deliberately withdrawn from production, milk quotas and, more recently, the 'de-coupling' (or disassociation) of the money farmers receive from the EU and the amount they produce (by the Fischler reforms in 2004). Agriculture expenditure will move away from subsidy payments linked to specific produce, toward direct payments based on farm size. This is intended to allow the market to dictate production levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stead_234-1"><a href="#cite_note-stead-234">[212]</a></sup> One of these reforms entailed the modification of the EU's sugar regime, which previously divided the sugar market between member states and certain African-Caribbean nations with a privileged relationship with the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC_CAP_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-EC_CAP-238">[215]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Labour_market">Labour market</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/EURES" title="EURES">EURES</a></div>
<p>The free movement of persons means that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_European_Union" title="Citizenship of the European Union">EU citizens</a> can move freely between member states to live, work, study or retire in another country. This required the lowering of administrative formalities and recognition of professional qualifications of other states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Single_Market_P_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Single_Market_P-239">[216]</a></sup>
</p><p>The EU seasonally adjusted unemployment rate was 6.7 per cent in September 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unemployment_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-unemployment-240">[217]</a></sup> The euro area unemployment rate was 8.1 per cent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unemployment_240-1"><a href="#cite_note-unemployment-240">[217]</a></sup> Among the member states, the lowest unemployment rates were recorded in the Czech Republic (2.3 per cent), Germany and Poland (both 3.4 per cent), and the highest in Spain (14.9 per cent) and Greece (19.0 in July 2018).&lt;/ref&gt;
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_and_monetary_union">Economic and monetary union</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_Monetary_Union_of_the_European_Union" title="Economic and Monetary Union of the European Union">Economic and Monetary Union of the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_European_Semester" title="The European Semester">The European Semester</a></div>
<p>The creation of a <a href="/wiki/European_Currency_Unit" title="European Currency Unit">European single currency</a> became an official objective of the European Economic Community in 1969. In 1992, having negotiated the structure and procedures of a currency union, the member states signed the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a> and were legally bound to fulfil the agreed-on rules including the <a href="/wiki/Euro_convergence_criteria" title="Euro convergence criteria">convergence criteria</a> if they wanted to join the <a href="/wiki/Currency_union" title="Currency union">monetary union</a>. The states wanting to participate had first to join the <a href="/wiki/European_Exchange_Rate_Mechanism" title="European Exchange Rate Mechanism">European Exchange Rate Mechanism</a>. To prevent the joining states from getting into financial trouble or crisis after entering the monetary union, they were obliged in the Maastricht treaty to fulfil important financial obligations and procedures, especially to show budgetary discipline and a high degree of sustainable economic convergence, as well as to avoid excessive government deficits and limit the government debt to a sustainable level, as agreed in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Fiscal_Pact" title="European Fiscal Pact">European Fiscal Pact</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_institutions_and_capital_markets_union">Financial institutions and capital markets union</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Capital_Markets_Union" title="Capital Markets Union">Capital Markets Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_System_of_Financial_Supervision" title="European System of Financial Supervision">European System of Financial Supervision</a></div>
<p>Free movement of capital is intended to permit movement of investments such as property purchases and buying of shares between countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Single_Market_C_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Single_Market_C-241">[218]</a></sup> Until the drive towards <a href="/wiki/Economic_and_monetary_union" title="Economic and monetary union">economic and monetary union</a> the development of the capital provisions had been slow. Post-Maastricht there has been a rapidly developing corpus of ECJ judgements regarding this initially neglected freedom. The free movement of capital is unique insofar as it is granted equally to non-member states.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_System_of_Financial_Supervision" title="European System of Financial Supervision">European System of Financial Supervision</a> is an institutional architecture of the EU's framework of financial supervision composed by three authorities: the <a href="/wiki/European_Banking_Authority" title="European Banking Authority">European Banking Authority</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Insurance_and_Occupational_Pensions_Authority" title="European Insurance and Occupational Pensions Authority">European Insurance and Occupational Pensions Authority</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Securities_and_Markets_Authority" title="European Securities and Markets Authority">European Securities and Markets Authority</a>. To complement this framework, there is also a <a href="/wiki/European_Systemic_Risk_Board" title="European Systemic Risk Board">European Systemic Risk Board</a> under the responsibility of the central bank. The aim of this financial control system is to ensure the economic stability of the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[219]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Eurozone_and_banking_union">Eurozone and banking union</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurosystem" title="Eurosystem">Eurosystem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurogroup" title="Eurogroup">Eurogroup</a>, <a href="/wiki/Euro_summit" title="Euro summit">Euro summit</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_banking_union" title="European banking union">European banking union</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_Stoxx_50" title="Euro Stoxx 50">Euro Stoxx 50</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eurobond_(eurozone)" title="Eurobond (eurozone)">Eurobond (eurozone)</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:120px;max-width:120px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:177px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:European_Central_Bank_Frankfurt_am_Main_IMG_0164.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="4656" data-file-width="3090" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/European_Central_Bank_Frankfurt_am_Main_IMG_0164.jpg/118px-European_Central_Bank_Frankfurt_am_Main_IMG_0164.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/European_Central_Bank_Frankfurt_am_Main_IMG_0164.jpg/177px-European_Central_Bank_Frankfurt_am_Main_IMG_0164.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/European_Central_Bank_Frankfurt_am_Main_IMG_0164.jpg/236px-European_Central_Bank_Frankfurt_am_Main_IMG_0164.jpg 2x" width="118"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:168px;max-width:168px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:177px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BlueEurozone.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="690" data-file-width="645" decoding="async" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/166px-BlueEurozone.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/249px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/BlueEurozone.svg/332px-BlueEurozone.svg.png 2x" width="166"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Left: The <a href="/wiki/Seat_of_the_European_Central_Bank" title="Seat of the European Central Bank">seat of the European Central Bank</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ostend_(Frankfurt_am_Main)" title="Ostend (Frankfurt am Main)">Ostend</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>. Right: 19 of the 27 EU member states have adopted the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> as their <a href="/wiki/Legal_tender" title="Legal tender">legal tender</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> (dark blue) represents 340 million people.</div></div></div></div>
<p>In 1999, the currency union started to materialise through introducing a common accounting (virtual) currency in <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_euro" title="History of the euro">eleven of the member states</a>. In 2002, it was turned into a fully-fledged conventible currency, when <a href="/wiki/Euro_banknotes" title="Euro banknotes">euro notes</a> and coins were issued, while the phaseout of national currencies in the eurozone (consisting by then of 12 member states) was initiated. The eurozone (constituted by the EU member states which have adopted the euro) has since grown to 19 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[220]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[x]</a></sup>
</p><p>19 member states known as the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> have fully implemented the currency union through supersededing their national currencies the single currency <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a>. The currency union represents 342<span class="nowrap"> </span>million EU citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_Single_Market_213-1"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_Single_Market-213">[193]</a></sup> The euro is the second largest <a href="/wiki/Reserve_currency" title="Reserve currency">reserve currency</a> as well as the second most traded currency in the world after the <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">United States dollar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[222]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[223]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Euro_Series_Banknotes_(2019).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="554" data-file-width="720" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Euro_Series_Banknotes_%282019%29.jpg/220px-Euro_Series_Banknotes_%282019%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Euro_Series_Banknotes_%282019%29.jpg/330px-Euro_Series_Banknotes_%282019%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Euro_Series_Banknotes_%282019%29.jpg/440px-Euro_Series_Banknotes_%282019%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Euro_Series_Banknotes_(2019).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> was introduced in 2002, replacing 12 national currencies. Seven countries have since joined.</div></div></div>
<p>The euro, and the monetary policies of those who have adopted it in agreement with the EU, are under the control of the ECB.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[224]</a></sup> The ECB is the central bank for the eurozone, and thus controls <a href="/wiki/Monetary_policy" title="Monetary policy">monetary policy</a> in that area with an agenda to maintain <a href="/wiki/Price_stability" title="Price stability">price stability</a>. It is at the centre of the <a href="/wiki/Eurosystem" title="Eurosystem">Eurosystem</a>, which comprehends all the Eurozone national central banks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ECB_org_197-1"><a href="#cite_note-ECB_org-197">[177]</a></sup>
</p><p>The ECB is also the central institution of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banking_Union" title="Banking Union">Banking Union</a> established within the eurozone and manages its <a href="/wiki/Single_Supervisory_Mechanism" title="Single Supervisory Mechanism">Single Supervisory Mechanism</a>. These is also a <a href="/wiki/Single_Resolution_Mechanism" title="Single Resolution Mechanism">Single Resolution Mechanism</a> in case of a bank default.
</p>
<h2><span id="Area_of_freedom.2C_security_and_justice"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Area_of_freedom,_security_and_justice">Area of freedom, security and justice</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Area_of_freedom,_security_and_justice" title="Area of freedom, security and justice">Area of freedom, security and justice</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_European_Union" title="Citizenship of the European Union">Citizenship of the European Union</a></div>
<p>Since the creation of the European Union in 1993, it has developed its competencies in the area of justice and home affairs; initially at an intergovernmental level and later by supranationalism. Accordingly, the union has legislated in areas such as <a href="/wiki/European_Arrest_Warrant" title="European Arrest Warrant">extradition</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[225]</a></sup> family law,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[226]</a></sup> asylum law,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[227]</a></sup> and criminal justice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[228]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Police_and_judicial_co-operation">Police and judicial co-operation</span></h3>
<p>The EU has also established agencies to co-ordinate police, prosecution and civil litigations across the member states: <a href="/wiki/Europol" title="Europol">Europol</a> for police co-operation, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CEPOL" title="CEPOL">CEPOL</a> for training of police forces<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[229]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Eurojust" title="Eurojust">Eurojust</a> for co-operation between prosecutors and courts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[230]</a></sup> It also operates the <a href="/wiki/EUCARIS" title="EUCARIS">EUCARIS</a> database of vehicles and drivers, the <a href="/wiki/Eurodac" title="Eurodac">Eurodac</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Criminal_Records_Information_System" title="European Criminal Records Information System">European Criminal Records Information System</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Cybercrime_Centre" title="European Cybercrime Centre">European Cybercrime Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/FADO" title="FADO">FADO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_Register_of_Travel_and_Identity_Documents_Online" title="Public Register of Travel and Identity Documents Online">PRADO</a> and others.
</p>
<h3><span id="Schengen_Area.2C_migration_and_asylum"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Schengen_Area,_migration_and_asylum">Schengen Area, migration and asylum</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cieszyneuro.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="566" data-file-width="750" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Cieszyneuro.JPG/220px-Cieszyneuro.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Cieszyneuro.JPG/330px-Cieszyneuro.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Cieszyneuro.JPG/440px-Cieszyneuro.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cieszyneuro.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Polish-Czech border in <a href="/wiki/Cieszyn" title="Cieszyn">Cieszyn</a>. Border control and identity checks have been abolished and the border facilities have been dismantled within the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>. The border is indicated with a simple road sign.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> and <a href="/wiki/Migration_and_asylum_policy_of_the_European_Union" title="Migration and asylum policy of the European Union">Migration and asylum policy of the European Union</a></div>
<p>The Schengen Area is an area comprising 26 <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> countries that have officially abolished all passport and all other types of <a href="/wiki/Border_control" title="Border control">border control</a> at their mutual borders. It mostly functions as a single jurisdiction under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visa_policies_in_the_European_Union" title="Visa policies in the European Union">a common visa policy</a> for international travel purposes. The area is named after the 1985 <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a> and the 1990 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schengen_Convention" title="Schengen Convention">Schengen Convention</a>, both signed in <a href="/wiki/Schengen,_Luxembourg" title="Schengen, Luxembourg">Schengen, Luxembourg</a>. The Area comprises 22 EU member states, the four states of the <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">European Free Trade Association</a> and several <a href="/wiki/European_microstates" title="European microstates">European microstates</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>The European Border and Coast Guard Agency (<a href="/wiki/Frontex" title="Frontex">Frontex</a>) is an <a href="/wiki/Agencies_of_the_European_Union" title="Agencies of the European Union">agency of the EU</a> aiming to detect and stop illegal immigration, <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">human trafficking</a> and terrorist infiltration, having since 2015 a stronger role and mandate along with national authorities for border management.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[231]</a></sup> The EU also operates the <a href="/wiki/European_Travel_Information_and_Authorisation_System" title="European Travel Information and Authorisation System">European Travel Information and Authorisation System</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Entry/Exit_System" title="Entry/Exit System">Entry/Exit System</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Information_System" title="Schengen Information System">Schengen Information System</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Visa_Information_System" title="Visa Information System">Visa Information System</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_European_Asylum_System" title="Common European Asylum System">Common European Asylum System</a> which provide common databases for police and immigration authorities. The impetus for the development of this co-operation was the advent of open borders in the Schengen Area and the associated cross-border crime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Internal_borders_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Internal_borders-20">[17]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px"><div style="width: 182px">

</p>

</div></li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Equality.2C_fundamental_rights_and_values"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Equality,_fundamental_rights_and_values">Equality, fundamental rights and values</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights_of_the_European_Union" title="Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union">Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:04CFREU-Article2-Crop.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1787" data-file-width="2669" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/04CFREU-Article2-Crop.jpg/220px-04CFREU-Article2-Crop.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/04CFREU-Article2-Crop.jpg/330px-04CFREU-Article2-Crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/04CFREU-Article2-Crop.jpg/440px-04CFREU-Article2-Crop.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:04CFREU-Article2-Crop.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights_of_the_European_Union" title="Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union">Charter of Fundamental Rights</a> contains a wide range of political, social, and economic rights for EU citizens.</div></div></div>
<p>Prohibitions against discrimination have a long standing in the treaties. In more recent years, these have been supplemented by powers to legislate against discrimination based on race, religion, disability, age, and sexual orientation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-art2(7)_Amsterdam_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-art2(7)_Amsterdam-256">[y]</a></sup> The treaties declare that the European Union itself is "founded on the values of respect for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_dignity" title="Human dignity">human dignity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberty" title="Liberty">freedom</a>, democracy, <a href="/wiki/Equality_before_the_law" title="Equality before the law">equality</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a> and respect for human rights, including the rights of persons belonging to <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">minorities</a> ... in a society in which pluralism, non-discrimination, tolerance, justice, solidarity and equality between women and men prevail."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[232]</a></sup> By virtue of these powers, the EU has enacted legislation on <a href="/wiki/Sexism" title="Sexism">sexism</a> in the work-place, <a href="/wiki/Ageism" title="Ageism">age discrimination</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Racism" title="Racism">racial discrimination</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[z]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lisbon_Treaty" title="Lisbon Treaty">Lisbon Treaty</a> gave legal effect to the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights_of_the_European_Union" title="Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union">Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union</a>. The charter is a codified catalogue of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fundamental_right" title="Fundamental right">fundamental rights</a> against which the EU's legal acts can be judged. It consolidates many rights which were previously recognised by the Court of Justice and derived from the "constitutional traditions common to the member states."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[233]</a></sup> The Court of Justice has long recognised fundamental rights and has, on occasion, invalidated EU legislation based on its failure to adhere to those fundamental rights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-europarl-rights_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-europarl-rights-260">[234]</a></sup>
</p><p>Signing the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a> (ECHR) is a condition for EU membership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[aa]</a></sup> Previously, the EU itself could not accede to the convention as it is neither a state<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[ab]</a></sup> nor had the competence to accede.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[ac]</a></sup> The Lisbon Treaty and Protocol 14 to the ECHR have changed this: the former binds the EU to accede to the convention while the latter formally permits it.
</p><p>The EU is independent from the Council of Europe, although they share purpose and ideas, especially on the rule of law, human rights and democracy. Furthermore, the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Social_Charter" title="European Social Charter">European Social Charter</a>, as well as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Source_of_law" title="Source of law">source of law</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights_of_the_European_Union" title="Charter of Fundamental Rights of the European Union">Charter of Fundamental Rights</a> are created by the Council of Europe. The EU has also promoted human rights issues in the wider world. The EU opposes the death penalty and has proposed its worldwide abolition. Abolition of the death penalty is a condition for EU membership.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[235]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 19 October 2020, the European Union revealed new plans to create a legal structure to act against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_rights_violations" title="Human rights violations">human rights violations</a> worldwide. The new plan was expected to provide the European Union with greater flexibility to target and sanction those responsible for serious human rights violations and abuses around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[236]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span id="Foreign_relations_.26_defence"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations_&amp;_defence">Foreign relations &amp; defence</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_European_Union" title="Foreign relations of the European Union">Foreign relations of the European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_Foreign_and_Security_Policy" title="Common Foreign and Security Policy">Common Foreign and Security Policy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/European_External_Action_Service" title="European External Action Service">European External Action Service</a></div>
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:602px"><div class="thumbimage noresize" style="width:600px;">

title="Armenia"/><area alt="Russia" coords="558,75,588,100" href="/wiki/Russia" shape="rect" title="Russia"/><area alt="Belarus" coords="558,32,588,60" href="/wiki/Belarus" shape="rect" title="Belarus"/><area alt="Serbia" coords="466,134,496,157" href="/wiki/Serbia" shape="rect" title="Serbia"/><area alt="Albania" coords="466,164,496,187" href="/wiki/Albania" shape="rect" title="Albania"/><area alt="North Macedonia" coords="428,164,458,187" href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" shape="rect" title="North Macedonia"/><area alt="Bosnia and Herzegovina" coords="428,197,458,219" href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" shape="rect" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina"/><area alt="Montenegro" coords="466,197,496,219" href="/wiki/Montenegro" shape="rect" title="Montenegro"/><area alt="Kosovo (UNMIK)" coords="510,197,540,219" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Interim_Administration_Mission_in_Kosovo" shape="rect" title="Kosovo (UNMIK)"/></map><img alt="Supranational European Bodies.svg" data-file-height="833" data-file-width="1205" decoding="async" height="415" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Supranational_European_Bodies.svg/600px-Supranational_European_Bodies.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Supranational_European_Bodies.svg/900px-Supranational_European_Bodies.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Supranational_European_Bodies.svg/1200px-Supranational_European_Bodies.svg.png 2x" usemap="#ImageMap_1ad7e6b849486dcf" width="600"/><div style="margin-left: 580px; margin-top: -20px; text-align: left;"><a href="/wiki/File:Supranational_European_Bodies-en.svg" title="About this image"><img alt="About this image" src="/w/extensions/ImageMap/resources/desc-20.png?15600" style="border: none;"/></a></div></div></div></div><div class="thumbcaption">A clickable <a href="/wiki/Euler_diagram" title="Euler diagram">Euler diagram</a><sup><a href="/wiki/File:Supranational_European_Bodies-en.svg" title="File:Supranational European Bodies-en.svg">[file]</a></sup> showing the relationships between various multinational European organisations and agreements. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1063604349" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini" style="float:right"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Supranational_European_Bodies" title="Template:Supranational European Bodies"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Supranational_European_Bodies" title="Template talk:Supranational European Bodies"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Supranational_European_Bodies&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Foreign policy co-operation between member states dates from the establishment of the community in 1957, when member states negotiated as a bloc in international trade negotiations under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU%27s_common_commercial_policy" title="EU's common commercial policy">EU's common commercial policy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[237]</a></sup> Steps for a more wide-ranging co-ordination in foreign relations began in 1970 with the establishment of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Political_Cooperation" title="European Political Cooperation">European Political Cooperation</a> which created an informal consultation process between member states with the aim of forming common foreign policies. In 1987 the European Political Cooperation was introduced on a formal basis by the <a href="/wiki/Single_European_Act" title="Single European Act">Single European Act</a>. EPC was renamed as the <a href="/wiki/Common_Foreign_and_Security_Policy" title="Common Foreign and Security Policy">Common Foreign and Security Policy</a> (CFSP) by the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EPC_267-0"><a href="#cite_note-EPC-267">[238]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Josep_Borrell_(49468484246).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3280" data-file-width="2183" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Josep_Borrell_%2849468484246%29.jpg/140px-Josep_Borrell_%2849468484246%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Josep_Borrell_%2849468484246%29.jpg/210px-Josep_Borrell_%2849468484246%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Josep_Borrell_%2849468484246%29.jpg/280px-Josep_Borrell_%2849468484246%29.jpg 2x" width="140"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Josep_Borrell_(49468484246).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Josep_Borrell" title="Josep Borrell">Josep Borrell</a>, <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy" title="High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy">High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The aims of the CFSP are to promote both the EU's own interests and those of the <a href="/wiki/International_community" title="International community">international community</a> as a whole, including the furtherance of international co-operation, respect for human rights, democracy, and the rule of law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-art11_Union_268-0"><a href="#cite_note-art11_Union-268">[239]</a></sup> The CFSP requires unanimity among the member states on the appropriate policy to follow on any particular issue. The unanimity and difficult issues treated under the CFSP sometimes lead to disagreements, such as those which occurred over the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">war in Iraq</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Iraq_statement_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Iraq_statement-269">[240]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:G7_leaders_on_Day_1_roundtable_meeting_at_Scholss_Elmau_Summit_(8).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1707" data-file-width="2600" decoding="async" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/G7_leaders_on_Day_1_roundtable_meeting_at_Scholss_Elmau_Summit_%288%29.jpg/220px-G7_leaders_on_Day_1_roundtable_meeting_at_Scholss_Elmau_Summit_%288%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/G7_leaders_on_Day_1_roundtable_meeting_at_Scholss_Elmau_Summit_%288%29.jpg/330px-G7_leaders_on_Day_1_roundtable_meeting_at_Scholss_Elmau_Summit_%288%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/G7_leaders_on_Day_1_roundtable_meeting_at_Scholss_Elmau_Summit_%288%29.jpg/440px-G7_leaders_on_Day_1_roundtable_meeting_at_Scholss_Elmau_Summit_%288%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:G7_leaders_on_Day_1_roundtable_meeting_at_Scholss_Elmau_Summit_(8).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The EU participates in all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Group_of_Seven" title="Group of Seven">G7</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G-20_major_economies" title="G-20 major economies">G20</a> summits. <a href="/wiki/48th_G7_summit" title="48th G7 summit">48th G7 summit</a> in <a href="/wiki/Schloss_Elmau" title="Schloss Elmau">Schloss Elmau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kr%C3%BCn" title="Krün">Krün</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Alps" title="Bavarian Alps">Bavarian Alps</a>, Germany, 2022.</div></div></div>
<p>The coordinator and representative of the CFSP within the EU is the <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy" title="High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy">high representative of the union for foreign affairs and security policy</a> who speaks on behalf of the EU in foreign policy and defence matters, and has the task of articulating the positions expressed by the member states on these fields of policy into a common alignment. The high representative heads up the <a href="/wiki/European_External_Action_Service" title="European External Action Service">European External Action Service</a> (EEAS), a unique EU department<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23Oct_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-23Oct-270">[241]</a></sup> that has been officially implemented and operational since 1 December 2010 on the occasion of the first anniversary of the entry into force of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[242]</a></sup> The EEAS will serve as a foreign ministry and <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_corps" title="Diplomatic corps">diplomatic corps</a> for the European Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_EEAS_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_EEAS-272">[243]</a></sup>
</p><p>Besides the emerging international policy of the European Union, the international influence of the EU is also felt through <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">enlargement</a>. The perceived benefits of becoming a member of the EU act as an incentive for both political and economic reform in states wishing to fulfil the EU's accession criteria, and are considered an important factor contributing to the reform of European formerly Communist countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[244]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 762">: 762 </span></sup> This influence on the internal affairs of other countries is generally referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Soft_power" title="Soft power">soft power</a>", as opposed to military "hard power".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Soft_Power_274-0"><a href="#cite_note-Soft_Power-274">[245]</a></sup>
</p><p>In some policies, there are several member states that ally with strategic partners within the union. Examples of such alliances include the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Assembly" title="Baltic Assembly">Baltic Assembly</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benelux_Union" title="Benelux Union">Benelux Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bucharest_Nine" title="Bucharest Nine">Bucharest Nine</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Craiova_Group" title="Craiova Group">Craiova Group</a>, the <a href="/wiki/EU_Med_Group" title="EU Med Group">EU Med Group</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lublin_Triangle" title="Lublin Triangle">Lublin Triangle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_Hanseatic_League" title="New Hanseatic League">New Hanseatic League</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Three_Seas_Initiative" title="Three Seas Initiative">Three Seas Initiative</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="Visegrád Group">Visegrád Group</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Triangle" title="Weimar Triangle">Weimar Triangle</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="External_security_and_defence">External security and defence</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Common_Security_and_Defence_Policy" title="Common Security and Defence Policy">Common Security and Defence Policy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Plus_agreement" title="Berlin Plus agreement">Berlin Plus agreement</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EU_and_NATO.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="520" data-file-width="680" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/EU_and_NATO.svg/220px-EU_and_NATO.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/EU_and_NATO.svg/330px-EU_and_NATO.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/EU_and_NATO.svg/440px-EU_and_NATO.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EU_and_NATO.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Of the 27 EU member states, 21 (shown purple) are also members of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>. Other colours: EU only (blue, including two EU members that are NATO applicants – Finland and Sweden) and NATO only (orange, including four NATO members that are EU applicants – Albania, Montenegro, Turkey and North Macedonia).</div></div></div>
<p>The predecessors of the European Union were not devised as a military alliance because <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> was largely seen as appropriate and sufficient for defence purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWilkinson2007100_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWilkinson2007100-275">[246]</a></sup> 21 EU members are members of NATO<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[247]</a></sup> while the remaining member states follow policies of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neutrality_(international_relations)" title="Neutrality (international relations)">neutrality</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[248]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Western_European_Union" title="Western European Union">Western European Union</a>, a military alliance with a mutual defence clause, was disbanded in 2010 as its role had been transferred to the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[249]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the withdrawal of the United Kingdom, France is the only member officially recognised as a <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_nuclear_weapons" title="List of states with nuclear weapons">nuclear weapon state</a> and the sole holder of a <a href="/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council">permanent seat</a> on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>. France and Italy are also the only EU countries that have <a href="/wiki/Power_projection" title="Power projection">power projection capabilities</a> outside of Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[250]</a></sup> Italy, Germany, the Netherlands and Belgium participate in NATO <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_sharing" title="Nuclear sharing">nuclear sharing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[251]</a></sup>
</p><p>Most EU member states opposed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">Nuclear Weapon Ban Treaty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[252]</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War" title="Kosovo War">Kosovo War</a> in 1999, the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> agreed that "the Union must have the capacity for autonomous action, backed by credible military forces, the means to decide to use them, and the readiness to do so, in order to respond to international crises without prejudice to actions by NATO". To that end, a number of efforts were made to increase the EU's military capability, notably the <a href="/wiki/Helsinki_Headline_Goal" title="Helsinki Headline Goal">Helsinki Headline Goal</a> process. After much discussion, the most concrete result was the <a href="/wiki/EU_Battlegroup" title="EU Battlegroup">EU Battlegroups</a> initiative, each of which is planned to be able to deploy quickly about 1500 personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Council_Capabilities_282-0"><a href="#cite_note-Council_Capabilities-282">[253]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_the_European_Union_Military_Staff.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="327" data-file-width="272" decoding="async" height="264" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Coat_of_arms_of_the_European_Union_Military_Staff.svg/220px-Coat_of_arms_of_the_European_Union_Military_Staff.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Coat_of_arms_of_the_European_Union_Military_Staff.svg/330px-Coat_of_arms_of_the_European_Union_Military_Staff.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Coat_of_arms_of_the_European_Union_Military_Staff.svg/440px-Coat_of_arms_of_the_European_Union_Military_Staff.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_the_European_Union_Military_Staff.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The coat of arms of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Military_Staff" title="European Union Military Staff">European Union Military Staff</a> (EUMS). The arms include Europe's crown of twelve golden stars, an anchor, wings and two crossed swords.</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EUFOR" title="EUFOR">EU forces</a> have been deployed on peacekeeping missions from middle and northern Africa to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Balkans" title="Western Balkans">western Balkans</a> and western Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Council_Operations_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-Council_Operations-283">[254]</a></sup> EU military operations are supported by a number of bodies, including the <a href="/wiki/European_Defence_Agency" title="European Defence Agency">European Defence Agency</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Satellite_Centre" title="European Union Satellite Centre">European Union Satellite Centre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Military_Staff" title="European Union Military Staff">European Union Military Staff</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Council_Structures_284-0"><a href="#cite_note-Council_Structures-284">[255]</a></sup> The European Union Military Staff is the highest military institution of the European Union, established within the framework of the European Council, and follows on from the decisions of the Helsinki European Council (10–11 December 1999), which called for the establishment of permanent political-military institutions. The European Union Military Staff is under the authority of the <a href="/wiki/High_Representative_of_the_Union_for_Foreign_Affairs_and_Security_Policy" title="High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy">High Representative of the Union for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy</a> and the Political and Security Committee. It directs all military activities in the EU context, including planning and conducting military missions and operations in the framework of the <a href="/wiki/Common_Security_and_Defence_Policy" title="Common Security and Defence Policy">Common Security and Defence Policy</a> and the development of military capabilities, and provides the Political and Security Committee with military advice and recommendations on military issues. In an EU consisting of 27 members, substantial security and defence co-operation is increasingly relying on collaboration among all member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[256]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Humanitarian_aid">Humanitarian aid</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Directorate-General_for_European_Civil_Protection_and_Humanitarian_Aid_Operations" title="Directorate-General for European Civil Protection and Humanitarian Aid Operations">Directorate-General for European Civil Protection and Humanitarian Aid Operations</a></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ECHO_(European_Commission)" title="ECHO (European Commission)">European Commission's Humanitarian Aid and Civil Protection department</a>, or "ECHO", provides <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian_aid" title="Humanitarian aid">humanitarian aid</a> from the EU to <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing countries</a>. In 2012, its budget amounted to €874<span class="nowrap"> </span>million, 51 per cent of the budget went to Africa and 20 per cent to Asia, Latin America, the Caribbean and Pacific, and 20 per cent to the Middle East and Mediterranean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[257]</a></sup>
</p><p>Humanitarian aid is financed directly by the budget (70 per cent) as part of the financial instruments for external action and also by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Development_Fund" title="European Development Fund">European Development Fund</a> (30 per cent).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI_287-0"><a href="#cite_note-ODI-287">[258]</a></sup> The EU's external action financing is divided into 'geographic' instruments and 'thematic' instruments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI_287-1"><a href="#cite_note-ODI-287">[258]</a></sup> The 'geographic' instruments provide aid through the <a href="/wiki/Development_Cooperation_Instrument" title="Development Cooperation Instrument">Development Cooperation Instrument</a> (DCI, €16.9<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion, 2007–2013), which must spend 95 per cent of its budget on <a href="/wiki/Official_development_assistance" title="Official development assistance">official development assistance</a> (ODA), and from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Neighbourhood_and_Partnership_Instrument" title="European Neighbourhood and Partnership Instrument">European Neighbourhood and Partnership Instrument</a> (ENPI), which contains some relevant programmes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI_287-2"><a href="#cite_note-ODI-287">[258]</a></sup> The European Development Fund (EDF, €22.7<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion for the period 2008–2013 and €30.5<span class="nowrap"> </span>billion for the period 2014–2020) is made up of voluntary contributions by member states, but there is pressure to merge the EDF into the budget-financed instruments to encourage increased contributions to match the 0.7 per cent target and allow the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> greater oversight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ODI_287-3"><a href="#cite_note-ODI-287">[258]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[259]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, the average among EU countries was 0.4 per cent and five had met or exceeded the 0.7 per cent target: Denmark, Germany, Luxembourg, Sweden and the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[260]</a></sup> If considered collectively, EU member states are the largest contributor of <a href="/wiki/List_of_development_aid_country_donors" title="List of development aid country donors">foreign aid</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GHA_report_2014_290-0"><a href="#cite_note-GHA_report_2014-290">[261]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OECD_aid_report_2013_291-0"><a href="#cite_note-OECD_aid_report_2013-291">[262]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_cooperation_and_development_partnerships">International cooperation and development partnerships</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Directorate-General_for_International_Cooperation_and_Development" title="Directorate-General for International Cooperation and Development">Directorate-General for International Cooperation and Development</a>, <a href="/wiki/ACP%E2%80%93EU_development_cooperation" title="ACP–EU development cooperation">ACP–EU development cooperation</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Solidarity_Corps" title="European Solidarity Corps">European Solidarity Corps</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Global_Strategy" title="European Union Global Strategy">European Union Global Strategy</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Neighbourhood_Policy" title="European Neighbourhood Policy">European Neighbourhood Policy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Global_Europe" title="Global Europe">Global Europe</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ilham_Aliyev_attended_EU_Eastern_Partnership_Summit_in_Brussels.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1400" data-file-width="2362" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Ilham_Aliyev_attended_EU_Eastern_Partnership_Summit_in_Brussels.jpg/220px-Ilham_Aliyev_attended_EU_Eastern_Partnership_Summit_in_Brussels.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Ilham_Aliyev_attended_EU_Eastern_Partnership_Summit_in_Brussels.jpg/330px-Ilham_Aliyev_attended_EU_Eastern_Partnership_Summit_in_Brussels.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Ilham_Aliyev_attended_EU_Eastern_Partnership_Summit_in_Brussels.jpg/440px-Ilham_Aliyev_attended_EU_Eastern_Partnership_Summit_in_Brussels.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ilham_Aliyev_attended_EU_Eastern_Partnership_Summit_in_Brussels.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Eastern_Partnership" title="Eastern Partnership">Eastern Partnership</a> Summit 2017, <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The European Union uses foreign relations instruments like the <a href="/wiki/European_Neighbourhood_Policy" title="European Neighbourhood Policy">European Neighbourhood Policy</a> which seeks to tie those countries to the east and south of the European territory of the EU to the union. These countries, primarily developing countries, include some who seek to one day become either a <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member state of the European Union</a>, or more closely integrated with the European Union. The EU offers financial assistance to countries within the European Neighbourhood, so long as they meet the strict conditions of government reform, economic reform and other issues surrounding positive transformation. This process is normally underpinned by an Action Plan, as agreed by both Brussels and the target country.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Membreupm.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="211" data-file-width="411" decoding="async" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Membreupm.png/220px-Membreupm.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Membreupm.png/330px-Membreupm.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/20/Membreupm.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Membreupm.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Union_for_the_Mediterranean" title="Union for the Mediterranean">Union for the Mediterranean</a> meeting in Barcelona.</div></div></div>
<p>There is also the worldwide <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Global_Strategy" title="European Union Global Strategy">European Union Global Strategy</a>. International recognition of sustainable development as a key element is growing steadily. Its role was recognised in three major UN summits on sustainable development: the 1992 <a href="/wiki/Earth_Summit" title="Earth Summit">UN Conference on Environment and Development</a> (UNCED) in Rio de Janeiro, Brazil; the 2002 World Summit on Sustainable Development (WSSD) in Johannesburg, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>; and the 2012 <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_Sustainable_Development" title="United Nations Conference on Sustainable Development">UN Conference on Sustainable Development</a> (UNCSD) in Rio de Janeiro. Other key global agreements are the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Agreement</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">2030 Agenda for Sustainable Development</a> (United Nations, 2015). The SDGs recognise that all countries must stimulate action in the following key areas – people, <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">planet</a>, prosperity, <a href="/wiki/Peace" title="Peace">peace</a> and <a href="/wiki/Partnership" title="Partnership">partnership</a> – in order to tackle the global challenges that are crucial for the survival of <a href="/wiki/Human" title="Human">humanity</a>.
</p><p>EU development action is based on the European Consensus on Development, which was endorsed on 20 December 2005 by EU Member States, the council, the European Parliament and the commission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[263]</a></sup> It is applied from the principles of <a href="/wiki/Capability_approach" title="Capability approach">Capability approach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rights-based_approach_to_development" title="Rights-based approach to development">Rights-based approach to development</a>. Funding is provided by the <a href="/wiki/Instrument_for_Pre-Accession_Assistance" title="Instrument for Pre-Accession Assistance">Instrument for Pre-Accession Assistance</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Global_Europe" title="Global Europe">Global Europe</a> programmes.
</p><p>Partnership and cooperation agreements are bilateral agreements with non-member nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pca_293-0"><a href="#cite_note-pca-293">[264]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Sustainability.2C_territorial_and_social_cohesion"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability,_territorial_and_social_cohesion">Sustainability, territorial and social cohesion</span></h2>
