<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/European_social_model" title="European social model">European social model</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Social_Fund" title="European Social Fund">European Social Fund</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Welfare_State" title="Welfare State">Welfare State</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Social_Charter" title="European Social Charter">European Social Charter</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Voluntary_Service" title="European Voluntary Service">European Voluntary Service</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_labour_law" title="European labour law">European labour law</a>, and <a href="/wiki/European_Pillar_of_Social_Rights" title="European Pillar of Social Rights">European Pillar of Social Rights</a></div>
<p>The European Union has long sought to mitigate the effects of free markets by protecting workers' rights and preventing <a href="/wiki/Social_dumping" title="Social dumping">social</a> and <a href="/wiki/Environmental_dumping" title="Environmental dumping">environmental dumping</a>. To this end it has adopted laws establishing minimum employment and environmental standards. These included the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Working_Time_Directive" title="Working Time Directive">Working Time Directive</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Impact_Assessment_Directive_2011" title="Environmental Impact Assessment Directive 2011">Environmental Impact Assessment Directive</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_rights_and_equality">Social rights and equality</span></h3>
<p>The EU has also sought to coordinate the social security and health systems of member states to facilitate individuals exercising free movement rights and to ensure they maintain their ability to access social security and health services in other member states. Social security main legislation is found in the Equal Treatment in Occupational Social Security Directive 86/378, the Equal Treatment in Social Security Directive 79/7/EEC, the Social Security Regulation 1408/71/EC and 883/2004/EC and the Directive 2005/36/EC.
</p><p>The European Directive about Minimum Wage, which looks to lift minimum wages and strengthen collective bargaining was approved by the European Parliament in September 2022<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[266]</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/European_unemployment_insurance" title="European unemployment insurance">European unemployment insurance</a> has been proposed among others by the commissioner of Jobs <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Schmit" title="Nicolas Schmit">Nicolas Schmit</a>.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296">[267]</a></sup> as well as a European Directive about Minimum Income.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto1_297-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-297">[268]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[269]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2019 there has been a European commissioner for equality and the <a href="/wiki/European_Institute_for_Gender_Equality" title="European Institute for Gender Equality">European Institute for Gender Equality</a> has existed since 2007. A Directive on countering gender-based violence has been proposed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299"><a href="#cite_note-299">[270]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[271]</a></sup> In September 2022, a European Care strategy was approved in order to provide "quality, affordable and accessible care services".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[272]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, the first ever European Union Strategy on LGBTIQ equality was approved under <a href="/wiki/Helena_Dalli" title="Helena Dalli">Helena Dalli</a> mandate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[273]</a></sup> In December 2021, the commission announced the intention of codifying a union-wide law against LGBT hate crimes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[274]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Social_Charter" title="European Social Charter">European Social Charter</a> is the main body that recognises the social rights of European citizens.
</p><p>Housing, youth, childhood, Functional diversity or elderly care are supportive competencies of the European Union and can be financed by the European Social Fund.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Pillar_of_Social_Rights" title="European Pillar of Social Rights">European Pillar of Social Rights</a> contains a preamble and 3 chapters with target values for 20 fields:
</p><p>Chapter I: Equal opportunities and access to the labour market
(general education, professional training and lifelong learning, gender equality, equal opportunities, active support for employment)
</p><p>Chapter II: Fair working conditions
(secure and adaptable employment, wages, information about employment conditions and protection in the event of dismissals, social dialogue and involvement of workers, work-life balance, healthy, safe and well-adapted working environments and data protection)
</p><p>Chapter III: Social protection and inclusion
(childcare and support for children, social protection, unemployment benefits, minimum income, old age income and pensions, healthcare, inclusion of people with disabilities, long-term care, housing and assistance for the homeless, access to essential services)
</p><p>The EPSR is intended to act as a reference document of sorts, by means of which the labour markets and social standards in the Member States may approach the standards defined in the Pillar in the long term.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[275]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_and_local_development">Regional and local development</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regional_policy_of_the_European_Union" title="Regional policy of the European Union">Regional policy of the European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Committee_of_the_Regions" title="European Committee of the Regions">European Committee of the Regions</a>, and <a href="/wiki/European_Investment_Bank" title="European Investment Bank">European Investment Bank</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:European_regional_policy_2014.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="609" decoding="async" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/European_regional_policy_2014.svg/220px-European_regional_policy_2014.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/European_regional_policy_2014.svg/330px-European_regional_policy_2014.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/European_regional_policy_2014.svg/440px-European_regional_policy_2014.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:European_regional_policy_2014.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Classification of regions from 2014 to 2020. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#FF0000; color:black;"> </span> Less developed regions</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#FFFF00; color:black;"> </span> Transition regions</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#0000FF; color:white;"> </span> More developed regions</div></div></div></div>
<p>The five <a href="/wiki/European_Structural_and_Investment_Funds" title="European Structural and Investment Funds">European Structural and Investment Funds</a> are supporting the development of the EU regions, primarily the underdeveloped ones, located mostly in the states of <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">central</a> and southern Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305">[276]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Business2000_Funds_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-Business2000_Funds-306">[277]</a></sup> Another fund (the <a href="/wiki/Instrument_for_Pre-Accession_Assistance" title="Instrument for Pre-Accession Assistance">Instrument for Pre-Accession Assistance</a>) provides support for candidate members to transform their country to conform to the EU's standard. Demographic transition to a society of ageing population, low fertility-rates and depopulation of non-metropolitan regions is tackled within this policies.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment_and_climate">Environment and climate</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Europe" title="Climate change in Europe">Climate change in Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Commissioner_for_the_Environment" title="European Commissioner for the Environment">European Commissioner for the Environment</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Climate_Change_Programme" title="European Climate Change Programme">European Climate Change Programme</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_LIFE_Programme" title="The LIFE Programme">The LIFE Programme</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Natura_2000" title="Natura 2000">Natura 2000</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="361" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg/220px-European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg/330px-European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg/440px-European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:European_Union_biogeography_countries.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Biogeography" title="Biogeography">Biogeographic regions</a> of the continental European Union, according to the <a href="/wiki/European_Environment_Agency" title="European Environment Agency">European Environmental Agency</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1957, when the European Economic Community was founded, it had no environmental policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJordanAdelle2012_307-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJordanAdelle2012-307">[278]</a></sup> Over the past 50 years, an increasingly dense network of legislation has been created, extending to all areas of environmental protection, including air pollution, water quality, waste management, nature conservation, and the control of chemicals, industrial hazards, and biotechnology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJordanAdelle2012_307-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJordanAdelle2012-307">[278]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_European_Environmental_Policy" title="Institute for European Environmental Policy">Institute for European Environmental Policy</a>, environmental law comprises over 500 Directives, Regulations and Decisions, making environmental policy a core area of European politics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-European_Environmental_Policy_2012_308-0"><a href="#cite_note-European_Environmental_Policy_2012-308">[279]</a></sup>
</p><p>European policy-makers originally increased the EU's capacity to act on environmental issues by defining it as a trade problem.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJordanAdelle2012_307-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJordanAdelle2012-307">[278]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Trade_barrier" title="Trade barrier">Trade barriers</a> and competitive distortions in the Common Market could emerge due to the different environmental standards in each member state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[280]</a></sup> In subsequent years, the environment became a formal policy area, with its own policy actors, principles and procedures. The legal basis for EU environmental policy was established with the introduction of the Single European Act in 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-European_Environmental_Policy_2012_308-1"><a href="#cite_note-European_Environmental_Policy_2012-308">[279]</a></sup>
</p><p>Initially, EU environmental policy focused on Europe. More recently, the EU has demonstrated leadership in global environmental governance, e.g. the role of the EU in securing the ratification and coming into force of the <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a> despite opposition from the United States. This international dimension is reflected in the EU's Sixth Environmental Action Programme,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[281]</a></sup> which recognises that its objectives can only be achieved if key international agreements are actively supported and properly implemented both at EU level and worldwide. The Lisbon Treaty further strengthened the leadership ambitions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJordanAdelle2012_307-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJordanAdelle2012-307">[278]</a></sup> EU law has played a significant role in improving habitat and species protection in Europe, as well as contributing to improvements in air and water quality and waste management.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-European_Environmental_Policy_2012_308-2"><a href="#cite_note-European_Environmental_Policy_2012-308">[279]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mitigating <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> is one of the top priorities of EU environmental policy. In 2007, member states agreed that, in the future, 20 per cent of the energy used across the EU must be <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable</a>, and carbon dioxide emissions have to be lower in 2020 by at least 20 per cent compared to 1990 levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EUO_energy_311-0"><a href="#cite_note-EUO_energy-311">[282]</a></sup> In 2017, the EU emitted 9.1 per cent of global <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenhouse-gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse-gas emissions">greenhouse-gas emissions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Global_Emissions_312-0"><a href="#cite_note-Global_Emissions-312">[283]</a></sup> The European Union claims that already in 2018, its GHG emissions were 23% lower that in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[284]</a></sup>
</p><p>The EU has adopted an <a href="/wiki/Emissions_trading" title="Emissions trading">emissions trading system</a> to incorporate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_emissions" title="Carbon emissions">carbon emissions</a> into the economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314">[285]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Green_Capital" title="European Green Capital">European Green Capital</a> is an annual award given to cities that focuses on the environment, energy efficiency, and quality of life in urban areas to create <a href="/wiki/Smart_city" title="Smart city">smart city</a>.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/2019_European_Parliament_election" title="2019 European Parliament election">2019 elections to the European Parliament</a>, the green parties increased their power, possibly because of the rise of post materialist values.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315">[286]</a></sup>
</p><p>Proposals to reach a zero carbon economy in the European Union by 2050 were suggested in 2018 – 2019. Almost all member states supported that goal at an EU summit in June 2019. The Czech Republic, Estonia, Hungary, and Poland disagreed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[287]</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2021 the European Union passed a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=European_Climate_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="European Climate Law (page does not exist)">European Climate Law</a> with targets of 55% GHG emissions reduction by 2030 and carbon neutrality by 2050.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317">[288]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2021 the European Union and the United States pledged to cut <a href="/wiki/Methane_emissions" title="Methane emissions">methane emissions</a> by 30% by 2030. The pledge is considered as a big achievement for climate change mitigation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[289]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span id="Culture.2C_education_.26_science"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture,_education_&amp;_science">Culture, education &amp; science</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:European_Capital_of_Culture.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="45" data-file-width="67" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/European_Capital_of_Culture.svg/220px-European_Capital_of_Culture.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/European_Capital_of_Culture.svg/330px-European_Capital_of_Culture.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/European_Capital_of_Culture.svg/440px-European_Capital_of_Culture.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:European_Capital_of_Culture.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The logo used by European Commission for <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a>.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Europe" title="Culture of Europe">Culture of Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Film_Awards" title="European Film Awards">European Film Awards</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cultural_policies_of_the_European_Union" title="Cultural policies of the European Union">Cultural policies of the European Union</a></div>
<p>Cultural co-operation between member states has been an interest of the European Union since its inclusion as a community competency in the Maastricht Treaty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bozoki_319-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bozoki-319">[290]</a></sup> Actions taken in the cultural area by the EU include the <a href="/wiki/Culture_2000" title="Culture 2000">Culture 2000</a> seven-year programme,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bozoki_319-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bozoki-319">[290]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/European_Cultural_Month" title="European Cultural Month">European Cultural Month</a> event,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Culture_Month_320-0"><a href="#cite_note-Culture_Month-320">[291]</a></sup> and orchestras such as the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Youth_Orchestra" title="European Union Youth Orchestra">European Union Youth Orchestra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[292]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> programme selects one or more cities in every year to assist the <a href="/wiki/Sociocultural_evolution" title="Sociocultural evolution">cultural development</a> of that city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Capital_Culture_322-0"><a href="#cite_note-Capital_Culture-322">[293]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_research">Education and research</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Educational_policies_and_initiatives_of_the_European_Union" title="Educational policies and initiatives of the European Union">Educational policies and initiatives of the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Framework_Programmes_for_Research_and_Technological_Development" title="Framework Programmes for Research and Technological Development">Framework Programmes for Research and Technological Development</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Holbein-erasmus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2290" data-file-width="1618" decoding="async" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Holbein-erasmus.jpg/170px-Holbein-erasmus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Holbein-erasmus.jpg/255px-Holbein-erasmus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Holbein-erasmus.jpg/340px-Holbein-erasmus.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Holbein-erasmus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Erasmus" title="Erasmus">Erasmus of Rotterdam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_humanism" title="Renaissance humanism">Renaissance humanist</a> after whom the <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Programme" title="Erasmus Programme">Erasmus Programme</a> is named</div></div></div>
<p>Basic education is an area where the EU's role is limited to supporting national governments. In higher education, the policy was developed in the 1980s in programmes supporting exchanges and mobility. The most visible of these has been the <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Programme" title="Erasmus Programme">Erasmus Programme</a>, a university exchange programme which began in 1987. In its first 20 years, it supported international exchange opportunities for well over 1.5 million university and college students and became a symbol of European student life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323"><a href="#cite_note-323">[294]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are similar programmes for school pupils and teachers, for trainees in <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">vocational education and training</a>, and for adult learners in the <a href="/wiki/Lifelong_Learning_Programme_2007%E2%80%932013" title="Lifelong Learning Programme 2007–2013">Lifelong Learning Programme 2007–2013</a>. These programmes are designed to encourage a wider knowledge of other countries and to spread good practices in the education and training fields across the EU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324"><a href="#cite_note-324">[295]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325">[296]</a></sup> Through its support of the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_Process" title="Bologna Process">Bologna Process</a>, the EU is supporting comparable standards and compatible degrees across Europe.
</p><p>Scientific development is facilitated through the EU's <a href="/wiki/Framework_Programmes_for_Research_and_Technological_Development" title="Framework Programmes for Research and Technological Development">Framework Programmes</a>, the first of which started in 1984. The aims of EU policy in this area are to co-ordinate and stimulate research. The independent <a href="/wiki/European_Research_Council" title="European Research Council">European Research Council</a> allocates EU funds to European or national research projects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326">[297]</a></sup> EU <a href="/wiki/Framework_Programmes_for_Research_and_Technological_Development" title="Framework Programmes for Research and Technological Development">research and technological framework programmes</a> deal in a number of areas, for example energy where the aim is to develop a diverse mix of <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> to help the environment and to reduce dependence on imported fuels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-327"><a href="#cite_note-327">[298]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_policies_of_the_European_Union" title="Sport policies of the European Union">Sport policies of the European Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:San_Siro_Stadium_in_the_2009-10_derby.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/San_Siro_Stadium_in_the_2009-10_derby.jpg/220px-San_Siro_Stadium_in_the_2009-10_derby.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/San_Siro_Stadium_in_the_2009-10_derby.jpg/330px-San_Siro_Stadium_in_the_2009-10_derby.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/San_Siro_Stadium_in_the_2009-10_derby.jpg/440px-San_Siro_Stadium_in_the_2009-10_derby.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:San_Siro_Stadium_in_the_2009-10_derby.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Football fans before a match (<a href="/wiki/San_Siro" title="San Siro">San Siro stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>Sport is mainly the responsibility of the member states or other international organisations, rather than of the EU. There are some EU policies that have affected sport, such as the free movement of workers, which was at the core of the <a href="/wiki/Bosman_ruling" title="Bosman ruling">Bosman ruling</a> that prohibited national football leagues from imposing quotas on foreign players with European citizenship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Boseman_328-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Boseman-328">[299]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a> requires any application of economic rules to take into account the specific nature of sport and its structures based on voluntary activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329"><a href="#cite_note-329">[300]</a></sup> This followed lobbying by governing organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> and <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>, due to objections over the application of free market principles to sport, which led to an increasing gap between rich and poor clubs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IHT_RT_330-0"><a href="#cite_note-IHT_RT-330">[301]</a></sup> The EU does fund a programme for Israeli, Jordanian, Irish, and British football coaches, as part of the Football 4 Peace project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-331"><a href="#cite_note-331">[302]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/European_Heritage_Label" title="European Heritage Label">European Heritage Label</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Europe" title="Flag of Europe">flag of Europe</a> consists of a <a href="/wiki/Circle_of_stars" title="Circle of stars">circle of</a> 12 golden stars on a blue background. Originally designed in 1955 for the Council of Europe, the flag was adopted by the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities" title="European Communities">European Communities</a>, the predecessors of the present European Union, in 1986. The Council of Europe gave the flag a symbolic description in the following terms,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36th_332-0"><a href="#cite_note-36th-332">[303]</a></sup> though the official symbolic description adopted by the EU omits the reference to the "Western world":<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1996guide_333-0"><a href="#cite_note-1996guide-333">[304]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Against the blue sky of the Western world, the stars symbolise the peoples of Europe in a form of a circle, the sign of union. The number of stars is invariably <a href="/wiki/12_(number)#Religion" title="12 (number)">twelve</a>, the figure twelve being the symbol of perfection and entirety.</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite>Council of Europe. Paris, 7–9 December 1955.</cite></div></blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Europa_copy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1081" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Europa_copy.jpg/150px-Europa_copy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Europa_copy.jpg/225px-Europa_copy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Europa_copy.jpg/300px-Europa_copy.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Europa_copy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Europa_(mythology)" title="Europa (mythology)">Europa</a> and the Bull on a Greek vase, circa 480 BC. <a href="/wiki/Tarquinia_National_Museum" title="Tarquinia National Museum">Tarquinia National Museum</a>, Italy</div></div></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Motto_of_the_European_Union" title="Motto of the European Union">United in Diversity</a></i> was adopted as the motto of the union in 2000, having been selected from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A_motto_for_Europe" title="A motto for Europe">proposals</a> submitted by school pupils.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESimons2002110_334-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESimons2002110-334">[305]</a></sup> Since 1985, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flag_day" title="Flag day">flag day</a> of the union has been <a href="/wiki/Europe_Day" title="Europe Day">Europe Day</a>, on 9 May (the date of the 1950 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schuman_declaration" title="Schuman declaration">Schuman declaration</a>). The <a href="/wiki/Anthem_of_Europe" title="Anthem of Europe">anthem of the EU</a> is an instrumental version of the prelude to the <i><a href="/wiki/Ode_to_Joy" title="Ode to Joy">Ode to Joy</a></i>, the 4th movement of <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Ludwig van Beethoven</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._9_(Beethoven)" title="Symphony No. 9 (Beethoven)">ninth symphony</a>. The anthem was adopted by European Community leaders in 1985 and has since been played on official occasions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-335"><a href="#cite_note-335">[306]</a></sup>
Besides naming the continent, the <a href="/wiki/Greek_mythology" title="Greek mythology">Greek mythological</a> figure of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Europa_(mythology)" title="Europa (mythology)">Europa</a> has frequently been employed as a <a href="/wiki/National_personification" title="National personification">personification</a> of Europe. Known from the myth in which <a href="/wiki/Zeus" title="Zeus">Zeus</a> seduces her in the guise of a white bull, Europa has also been referred to in relation to the present union. Statues of Europa and the bull decorate several of the EU's institutions and a portrait of her is seen on the 2013 series of <a href="/wiki/Euro_banknotes" title="Euro banknotes">euro banknotes</a>. The bull is, for its part, depicted on all residence permit cards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDemey2007387_336-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDemey2007387-336">[307]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charles the Great</a>, also known as Charlemagne (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la">Carolus Magnus</i>) and later recognised as <i>Pater Europae</i> ("Father of Europe"),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_337-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-337">[308]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-338"><a href="#cite_note-338">[309]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-339"><a href="#cite_note-339">[310]</a></sup> has a symbolic relevance to Europe. The commission has named <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne_building" title="Charlemagne building">one of its central buildings</a> in Brussels after Charlemagne and the city of <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a> has since 1949 awarded the <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne_Prize" title="Charlemagne Prize">Charlemagne Prize</a> to champions of European unification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340"><a href="#cite_note-340">[311]</a></sup> Since 2008, the organisers of this prize, in conjunction with the European Parliament, have awarded the <a href="/wiki/European_Charlemagne_Youth_Prize" title="European Charlemagne Youth Prize">Charlemagne Youth Prize</a> in recognition of similar efforts led by young people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-341"><a href="#cite_note-341">[312]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Media_freedom_in_the_European_Union" title="Media freedom in the European Union">Media freedom in the European Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Broadcasting_Union" title="European Broadcasting Union">European Broadcasting Union</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1366" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg/220px-Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg/330px-Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg/440px-Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Si%C3%A8ge_d%27Euronews.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Euronews" title="Euronews">Euronews</a> headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a>, France</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_freedom" title="Media freedom">Media freedom</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Fundamental_rights" title="Fundamental rights">fundamental right</a> that applies to all <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member states</a> of the European Union and its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU_citizens" title="EU citizens">citizens</a>, as defined in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU_Charter_of_Fundamental_Rights" title="EU Charter of Fundamental Rights">EU Charter of Fundamental Rights</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eprs_342-0"><a href="#cite_note-eprs-342">[313]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 1">: 1 </span></sup> Within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EU_enlargement" title="EU enlargement">EU enlargement</a> process, guaranteeing media freedom is named a "key indicator of a country's readiness to become part of the EU".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-343"><a href="#cite_note-343">[314]</a></sup>
</p><p>The majority of media in the European Union are national-orientated, although some EU-wide media focusing on European affairs have emerged since the early 1990s, such as <a href="/wiki/Euronews" title="Euronews">Euronews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurosport" title="Eurosport">Eurosport</a>, <a href="/wiki/EUobserver" title="EUobserver">EUobserver</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EURACTIV" title="EURACTIV">EURACTIV</a> or <a href="/wiki/Politico_Europe" title="Politico Europe">Politico Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-344"><a href="#cite_note-344">[315]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-345"><a href="#cite_note-345">[316]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arte" title="Arte">ARTE</a> is a public Franco-German TV network that promotes programming in the areas of culture and the arts. 80 per cent of its programming are provided in equal proportion by the two member companies, while the remainder is being provided by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Economic_Interest_Grouping" title="European Economic Interest Grouping">European Economic Interest Grouping</a> <i>ARTE GEIE</i> and the channel's European partners.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-346"><a href="#cite_note-346">[317]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MEDIA_Programme" title="MEDIA Programme">MEDIA Programme</a> of the European Union has supported the European popular film and audiovisual industries since 1991. It provides support for the development, promotion and distribution of European works within Europe and beyond.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-347"><a href="#cite_note-347">[318]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence">Influence</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2816" data-file-width="1880" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg/170px-Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg/255px-Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg/340px-Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eiffel_Tower_wearing_Europe_colors_-_panoramio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Europe" title="Flag of Europe">European emblem</a> emblazoned on the <a href="/wiki/Eiffel_Tower" title="Eiffel Tower">Eiffel Tower</a></div></div></div>
<p>The European Union has had a significant positive economic effect on most member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JoME_348-0"><a href="#cite_note-JoME-348">[319]</a></sup> According to a 2019 study of the member states who joined from 1973 to 2004, "without European integration, per capita incomes would have been, on average, approximately 10 per cent lower in the first ten years after joining the EU."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JoME_348-1"><a href="#cite_note-JoME-348">[319]</a></sup> Greece was the exception reported by the study, which analysed up to 2008, "to avoid confounding effects from the global financial crisis".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JoME_348-2"><a href="#cite_note-JoME-348">[319]</a></sup> A 2021 study in the <i>Journal of Political Economy</i> found that the 2004 enlargement had aggregate beneficial economic effects on all groups in both the old and new member states. The largest winners were the new member states, in particular unskilled labour in the new member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-349"><a href="#cite_note-349">[320]</a></sup>
</p><p>The European Union has contributed to peace in Europe, in particular by pacifying border disputes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-350"><a href="#cite_note-350">[321]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-351"><a href="#cite_note-351">[322]</a></sup> and to the spread of democracy, especially by encouraging democratic reforms in aspiring Eastern European member states after the collapse of the USSR.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-352"><a href="#cite_note-352">[323]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_353-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-353">[324]</a></sup> Scholar <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Risse" title="Thomas Risse">Thomas Risse</a> wrote in 2009, "there is a consensus in the literature on Eastern Europe that the EU membership perspective had a huge anchoring effects for the new democracies."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_353-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-353">[324]</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/R._Daniel_Kelemen" title="R. Daniel Kelemen">R. Daniel Kelemen</a> argues that the EU has proved beneficial to leaders who are overseeing <a href="/wiki/Democratic_backsliding" title="Democratic backsliding">democratic backsliding</a>, as the EU is reluctant to intervene in domestic politics, gives authoritarian governments funds which they can use to strengthen their regimes, and because freedom of movement within the EU allows dissenting citizens to leave their backsliding countries. At the same time, the union provides an external constraint that prevents soft authoritarian regimes from progressing into hard dictatorships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-354"><a href="#cite_note-354">[325]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-Supremacy-149"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Supremacy_149-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to the principle of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Law_of_the_European_Union#Supremacy" title="Law of the European Union">supremacy</a> as established by the ECJ in Case 6/64, <i>Falminio Costa v. ENEL</i> [1964] ECR 585. See Craig and de Búrca, ch. 7. See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Factortame_litigation" title="Factortame litigation">Factortame litigation</a>: <i>Factortame Ltd. v. Secretary of State for Transport (No. 2) [1991] 1 AC 603</i>, <i>Solange II</i> (<i>Re Wuensche Handelsgesellschaft</i>, BVerfG decision of 22 October 1986 [1987] 3 CMLR 225,265) and <i>Frontini v. Ministero delle Finanze</i> [1974] 2 CMLR 372; <i>Raoul George Nicolo</i> [1990] 1 CMLR 173.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-art249-152"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-art249_152-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-art249_152-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">See Article 288 (ex Article 249 TEC) of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union, on <a class="external text" href="http://eur-lex.europa.eu/LexUriServ/LexUriServ.do?uri=OJ:C:2010:083:0047:0200:EN:PDF" rel="nofollow">eur-lex.europa.eu</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20191025183651/http://eur-lex.europa.eu/LexUriServ/LexUriServ.do?uri=OJ:C:2010:083:0047:0200:EN:PDF" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 25 October 2019 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Direct_Effect-153"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Direct_Effect_153-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to the principle of Direct Effect first invoked in the Court of Justice's decision in <cite><i><a href="/wiki/Van_Gend_en_Loos_v_Nederlandse_Administratie_der_Belastingen" title="Van Gend en Loos v Nederlandse Administratie der Belastingen">Van Gend en Loos v Nederlandse Administratie der Belastingen</a></i></cite>, <a class="external text" href="http://eur-lex.europa.eu/LexUriServ/LexUriServ.do?uri=CELEX:61962J0026:EN:NOT" rel="nofollow"> Eur-Lex</a> (European Court of Justice 1963). See: Craig and de Búrca, ch. 5.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-155"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-155">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See: Case 34/73, <i>Variola v. Amministrazione delle Finanze</i> <a class="external text" href="http://eur-lex.europa.eu/LexUriServ/LexUriServ.do?uri=CELEX:61973J0034:EN:NOT" rel="nofollow">[1973] ECR 981</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-156"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-156">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">To do otherwise would require the drafting of legislation which would have to cope with the frequently divergent legal systems and administrative systems of all of the now 28 member states. See Craig and de Búrca, p. 115</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-215"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-215">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Article 3(1)(g) of the Treaty of Rome</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-218"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-218">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Almost all uranium is imported and nuclear power is considered primary energy produced in the EU.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-235"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-235">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Article 39 (ex Article 33) of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union, on <a class="external text" href="http://arquivo.pt/wayback/20131106072048/http://eur-lex.europa.eu/LexUriServ/LexUriServ.do?uri=OJ%3AC%3A2010%3A083%3A0047%3A0200%3AEN%3APDF" rel="nofollow">eur-lex.europa.eu</a></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-146"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-146">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Burgess, Michael (2000). Federalism and European union: The building of Europe, 1950–2000. Routledge. p. 49. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-415-22647-3" title="Special:BookSources/0-415-22647-3">0-415-22647-3</a>.
